Definition of Tadbir and Its Pillar
Defining tadbir and stating its pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tadbir and identify its pillar.

Core Idea
Tadbir is the suspension of a slave's freedom upon the master's absolute death; its pillar is the verbal expression.

Tadbir is a distinct form of manumission that takes effect only after the master's death. In this lesson, we explore its meaning from both a linguistic and a juristic perspective, and we learn that the essential pillar of tadbir is the spoken declaration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning of tadbir
Tadbir linguistically means 'freeing after death' or 'reflecting on consequences'. This helps understand the legal concept.
2
Identify the juristic meaning
Juristicly, tadbir is the suspension of manumission upon the master's death through specific wording.
3
Recognize the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is the verbal expression that clearly indicates the meaning of tadbir, e.g., 'you are free when I die'. Without it, tadbir does not exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التدبير هو تعليق العتق بمطلق موته كإذا مت فأنت حر وأنت حر يوم أموت أو عن دبر وقدمناه باب التدبير هـ. ما بيان للعتق الواقع بعد الموت بعد ما بين الواقع في الحياة، وقدمه على الاستيلاد لشموله الذكر والأنثى. وله معنيان لغوي وفقهي ؛ فالأول كما في المغرب الإعتاق عن دبر وهو بعد الموت، وتدبر في الأمر نظر في ادباره أي في عواقبه ا وفي ضياء الحلوم: التدبير عتق العبد والأمة بعد الموت وتدبير الأمر النظر فيه إلى ما تصير إليه العاقبة ا هـ . والثاني ما ذكره الشيخ رحمه الله تعالى وركنه اللفظ الدال على معناه وشرائطه نوعان: عام وخاص ؛ فالعام من شرائط العتق فلا يصح إلا من الأهل في المحل منجزاً أو معلقاً أو مضافاً، سواء كان إلى وقت أو إلى الملك أو إلى سببه . والخاص تعليقه بموت المولى فلو علقه بموت غيره لا يكون مدبراً. وأن يكون بمطلق ،موته وأن يكون بموته وحده كما سيأتي، وأما صفته فالتجزي عنده خلافاً لهما، فلو دبره أحدهما اقتصر على نصيبه وللآخر عند يسار شریکه ست خيارات الخمسة المتقدمة والترك على حاله كما عرف في البدائع. وسيأتي بيان أحكامه من عدم جواز إخراجه عن الملك في حالة الحياة ومن عتقه من الثلث بعد موت المولى إلى آخره قوله : (وهو تعليق العتق بمطلق موته أي موت المولى فخرج بقيد الإطلاق التدبير المقيد كتعليقه بموت موصوف بصفة كما سيأتي وكذا التعليق بموته وموت غيره، وخرج أيضاً أنت حر بعد موتي بيوم أو بشهر فهو وصية بالإعتاق فلا يعتق بعد موت المولى إلا بإعتاق الوارث أو الوصي كما في الذخيرة. وخرج بموته تعليقه بموت غيره كقوله إن مات باب التدبير قوله : (فإنه يعتق بعد موته ظاهره أنه يعتق كله مع أنه صرح في الفتح فيما لو أوصى لعبده
Chapter on Tadbir: It is the suspension of manumission upon his absolute death, such as 'If I die, you are free' and 'You are free on the day I die' or 'after death'. We have preceded the chapter on tadbir - end. What is an explanation of the manumission occurring after death, after what was explained of manumission in life, and he gave it precedence over istilad because it includes male and female. It has two meanings: linguistic and juristic. The first, as in al-Mughrib: manumission after death, and tadbir in an affair is looking into its consequences. In Diya' al-Hulm: Tadbir is the manumission of a slave or slave-girl after death, and tadbir of an affair is reflecting on what the outcome leads to. End. The second is what the author (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned: its pillar is the verbal expression indicating its meaning, and its conditions are of two types: general and specific. The general: from the conditions of manumission, so it is only valid from one who is eligible, regarding a proper subject, whether immediate, suspended, or added, whether to a time, to ownership, or to its cause. The specific: its suspension upon the master's death; if he suspends it upon another's death, it is not tadbir. And it must be absolute of his death, and it must be upon his death alone, as will come. As for its description: partiality according to him, contrary to the two. So if one of two co-owners makes tadbir, it is confined to his share, and the other, if his partner is wealthy, has six options, the five previously mentioned, and leaving it as is, as known in al-Bada'i. The explanation of its rulings will come: the prohibition of removing it from ownership during life, and its manumission from one-third after the master's death, etc. His saying: (It is the suspension of manumission upon his absolute death) i.e., the master's death. So by the restriction 'absolute' is excluded restricted tadbir, like suspending it upon a death described with a quality, as will come, and similarly suspension upon his death and the death of another. Also excluded is 'you are free after my death by a day or a month', for that is a wasiyyah (bequest) of manumission, so he is not free after the master's death except by the manumission of the heir or executor, as in al-Dhakhirah. Also excluded by 'his death' is suspension upon the death of another, like his saying 'if he dies' – chapter on tadbir. His saying: (Then he is free after his death; its apparent meaning is that he is entirely free, although he stated in al-Fath that if he bequeaths to his slave...
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on tadbir (postponed manumission) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Tadbir is defined as the suspension of a slave's manumission upon the absolute death of the master. The author explains that the term has two meanings: linguistic (freeing after death) and juristic (the specific legal act). The pillar (rukn) of tadbir is the verbal expression that clearly indicates the meaning, such as 'you are free when I die' or 'you are free on the day of my death'. The conditions are divided into two categories: general and specific. The general conditions are those applicable to any valid manumission: the declarant must be eligible (adult, sane, owner), the subject must be a valid slave, and the declaration may be immediate (munajjaz), suspended (mu'allaq), or added (mudaf) to a time or ownership. The specific conditions are unique to tadbir: the suspension must be upon the master's own death, not another's, and it must be absolute (not qualified with a condition like 'if he dies in Hajj'). The text then discusses the issue of partial tadbir (tujzi') when one co-owner makes a declaration. According to Abu Hanifa, partial tadbir is valid and applies only to his share; the other co-owner has several options (such as buying the share, freeing, etc.). This is contrary to the Sahibayn who do not allow partial tadbir. The passage also distinguishes tadbir from a bequest of manumission (wasiyyah bil-i'tq). For instance, if one says 'you are free a day after my death', it is a bequest, not tadbir, and requires the heir's or executor's action. The text cuts off while discussing a point from Fath al-Qadir about a master who bequeaths his slave.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A form of manumission where the slave's freedom is suspended upon the master's death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose owner has declared tadbir.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal effect upon a future event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the pillar (rukn) of tadbir according to the Hanafi school?
A) The master's death
B) The slave's acceptance
C) The verbal expression indicating tadbir
D) The presence of witnesses

Key Takeaway
Tadbir is defined as the suspension of manumission upon the master's death, and its pillar is the verbal expression indicating this meaning.

General Conditions of Tadbir
Explaining the general conditions of tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the general conditions of tadbir and explain why they are the same as those for manumission.

Core Idea
Tadbir shares the general conditions of manumission: valid only from eligible owner over a proper subject, in immediate, suspended, or added form.

Tadbir is a form of manumission, so it inherits the general conditions of manumission. In this lesson, we examine these conditions, which include the declarant's eligibility, the subject's status, and the nature of the declaration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of conditions
The author divides tadbir's conditions into general and specific. General are shared with manumission.
2
List the general conditions
General conditions: declarant must be eligible (owner, adult, sane), subject must be a valid slave, and declaration can be immediate, suspended, or added.
3
Apply the conditions to a scenario
If any general condition is missing, tadbir is invalid. For example, if a non-owner declares tadbir, it is void.

Source Text

Key Terms
منجز (munajjaz): Immediate; a declaration that takes effect immediately.
معلق (mu'allaq): Suspended upon a future condition.
مضاف (mudaf): Added to a future time or ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a general condition of tadbir?
A) The declarant must be the owner
B) The declaration must be in writing
C) The slave must be a valid subject for manumission
D) The declaration can be immediate or suspended

Key Takeaway
The general conditions of tadbir are identical to those of regular manumission: eligible declarant, proper subject, and any valid form of declaration.

Specific Conditions of Tadbir
Laying out the specific conditions of tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific conditions of tadbir and distinguish it from a bequest of manumission.

Core Idea
Tadbir requires suspension upon the master's own absolute death; any qualification or attachment to another's death invalidates it.

While general conditions are shared with manumission, tadbir has unique specific conditions that define its nature. In this lesson, we explore these conditions: the suspension must be upon the master's own death, must be absolute (not qualified), and must be upon his death alone. We also learn how tadbir differs from a simple bequest of manumission.

Guided Path
1
First specific condition: master's own death
The suspension must be upon the death of the master himself. If tied to another's death, it is not tadbir.
2
Second: absolute death
The suspension must be absolute (mullaq), not qualified with a condition like 'if I die in travel'.
Absolute means without any additional condition.
3
Third: death alone
The suspension must be upon the master's death alone, not combined with another event (e.g., 'when I die and my wife dies').
4
Distinguish from bequest
If the expression refers to freedom after death by a day or month, it is a wasiyyah, not tadbir. The slave is not freed automatically.
Bequest requires action by heirs or executor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
مطلق الموت (mullaq al-mawt): Absolute death, without any qualification or condition.
وصية بالعتق (wasiyyah bil-i'tq): A bequest of manumission; a slave is to be freed after the master's death as part of the bequeathable third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid tadbir?
A) 'You are free when my son dies'
B) 'You are free when I die if I am on Hajj'
C) 'You are free when I die'
D) 'You are free a month after my death'

Key Takeaway
Tadbir requires three specific conditions: suspension upon the master's own death, absolute (unqualified), and alone; any delay or condition turns it into a bequest.

Partial Tadbir: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tujzi'
Discussing the validity of partial tadbir in co-ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on partial tadbir and identify the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits partial tadbir (tujzi') where one co-owner's declaration frees only his share; the Sahibayn require full tadbir.

When two co-owners own a slave and one declares tadbir, a dispute arises: does the tadbir apply only to his share (Abu Hanifa) or is it invalid unless both agree (Sahibayn)? This lesson examines both positions and the practical options for the non-declaring co-owner.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Two co-owners own a slave; one declares tadbir for his share.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
Partial tadbir is valid; it affects only the declarant's share.
3
State the Sahibayn's view
Tadbir must be comprehensive; partial tadbir is invalid.
4
Note the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the non-declaring co-owner has options (free his share, buy out, etc.). Under Sahibayn, nothing happens unless both agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التدبير هو تعليق العتق بمطلق موته كإذا مت فأنت حر وأنت حر يوم أموت أو عن دبر وقدمناه باب التدبير هـ. ما بيان للعتق الواقع بعد الموت بعد ما بين الواقع في الحياة، وقدمه على الاستيلاد لشموله الذكر والأنثى. وله معنيان لغوي وفقهي ؛ فالأول كما في المغرب الإعتاق عن دبر وهو بعد الموت، وتدبر في الأمر نظر في ادباره أي في عواقبه ا وفي ضياء الحلوم: التدبير عتق العبد والأمة بعد الموت وتدبير الأمر النظر فيه إلى ما تصير إليه العاقبة ا هـ . والثاني ما ذكره الشيخ رحمه الله تعالى وركنه اللفظ الدال على معناه وشرائطه نوعان: عام وخاص ؛ فالعام من شرائط العتق فلا يصح إلا من الأهل في المحل منجزاً أو معلقاً أو مضافاً، سواء كان إلى وقت أو إلى الملك أو إلى سببه . والخاص تعليقه بموت المولى فلو علقه بموت غيره لا يكون مدبراً. وأن يكون بمطلق ،موته وأن يكون بموته وحده كما سيأتي، وأما صفته فالتجزي عنده خلافاً لهما، فلو دبره أحدهما اقتصر على نصيبه وللآخر عند يسار شریکه ست خيارات الخمسة المتقدمة والترك على حاله كما عرف في البدائع. وسيأتي بيان أحكامه من عدم جواز إخراجه عن الملك في حالة الحياة ومن عتقه من الثلث بعد موت المولى إلى آخره قوله : (وهو تعليق العتق بمطلق موته أي موت المولى فخرج بقيد الإطلاق التدبير المقيد كتعليقه بموت موصوف بصفة كما سيأتي وكذا التعليق بموته وموت غيره، وخرج أيضاً أنت حر بعد موتي بيوم أو بشهر فهو وصية بالإعتاق فلا يعتق بعد موت المولى إلا بإعتاق الوارث أو الوصي كما في الذخيرة. وخرج بموته تعليقه بموت غيره كقوله إن مات باب التدبير قوله : (فإنه يعتق بعد موته ظاهره أنه يعتق كله مع أنه صرح في الفتح فيما لو أوصى لعبده
Chapter on Tadbir: It is the suspension of manumission upon his absolute death, such as 'If I die, you are free' and 'You are free on the day I die' or 'after death'. We have preceded the chapter on tadbir - end. What is an explanation of the manumission occurring after death, after what was explained of manumission in life, and he gave it precedence over istilad because it includes male and female. It has two meanings: linguistic and juristic. The first, as in al-Mughrib: manumission after death, and tadbir in an affair is looking into its consequences. In Diya' al-Hulm: Tadbir is the manumission of a slave or slave-girl after death, and tadbir of an affair is reflecting on what the outcome leads to. End. The second is what the author (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned: its pillar is the verbal expression indicating its meaning, and its conditions are of two types: general and specific. The general: from the conditions of manumission, so it is only valid from one who is eligible, regarding a proper subject, whether immediate, suspended, or added, whether to a time, to ownership, or to its cause. The specific: its suspension upon the master's death; if he suspends it upon another's death, it is not tadbir. And it must be absolute of his death, and it must be upon his death alone, as will come. As for its description: partiality according to him, contrary to the two. So if one of two co-owners makes tadbir, it is confined to his share, and the other, if his partner is wealthy, has six options, the five previously mentioned, and leaving it as is, as known in al-Bada'i. The explanation of its rulings will come: the prohibition of removing it from ownership during life, and its manumission from one-third after the master's death, etc. His saying: (It is the suspension of manumission upon his absolute death) i.e., the master's death. So by the restriction 'absolute' is excluded restricted tadbir, like suspending it upon a death described with a quality, as will come, and similarly suspension upon his death and the death of another. Also excluded is 'you are free after my death by a day or a month', for that is a wasiyyah (bequest) of manumission, so he is not free after the master's death except by the manumission of the heir or executor, as in al-Dhakhirah. Also excluded by 'his death' is suspension upon the death of another, like his saying 'if he dies' – chapter on tadbir. His saying: (Then he is free after his death; its apparent meaning is that he is entirely free, although he stated in al-Fath that if he bequeaths to his slave...
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on tadbir (postponed manumission) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Tadbir is defined as the suspension of a slave's manumission upon the absolute death of the master. The author explains that the term has two meanings: linguistic (freeing after death) and juristic (the specific legal act). The pillar (rukn) of tadbir is the verbal expression that clearly indicates the meaning, such as 'you are free when I die' or 'you are free on the day of my death'. The conditions are divided into two categories: general and specific. The general conditions are those applicable to any valid manumission: the declarant must be eligible (adult, sane, owner), the subject must be a valid slave, and the declaration may be immediate (munajjaz), suspended (mu'allaq), or added (mudaf) to a time or ownership. The specific conditions are unique to tadbir: the suspension must be upon the master's own death, not another's, and it must be absolute (not qualified with a condition like 'if he dies in Hajj'). The text then discusses the issue of partial tadbir (tujzi') when one co-owner makes a declaration. According to Abu Hanifa, partial tadbir is valid and applies only to his share; the other co-owner has several options (such as buying the share, freeing, etc.). This is contrary to the Sahibayn who do not allow partial tadbir. The passage also distinguishes tadbir from a bequest of manumission (wasiyyah bil-i'tq). For instance, if one says 'you are free a day after my death', it is a bequest, not tadbir, and requires the heir's or executor's action. The text cuts off while discussing a point from Fath al-Qadir about a master who bequeaths his slave.

Key Terms
تجزي (tujzi'): Partiality; the quality of being divisible. Here, the ability to declare tadbir for a partial share.
اختيارات (ikhtiyarat): Options; the choices available to the non-declaring co-owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, if one co-owner declares tadbir for his share, what is the effect?
A) The tadbir is invalid
B) The entire slave becomes mudabbar
C) Only the declarant's share becomes mudabbar
D) The slave is freed immediately

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa permits partial tadbir (tujzi'), giving the non-declaring co-owner several options; the Sahibayn require full tadbir.

Definition and Conditions of Tadbir
Defines tadbir linguistically and technically, lists conditions, and contrasts with wasiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tadbir, identify its conditions, and distinguish it from wasiyya.

Core Idea
Tadbir is a conditional emancipation attached exclusively to the master's absolute death.

Tadbir (making a slave a mudabbar) is a unique form of emancipation in Hanafi fiqh, combining elements of conditional contracts and bequests. This lesson unpacks its linguistic and technical definitions, its essential conditions, and how it differs from a bequest of emancipation (wasiyya). Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying tadbir rules.

Guided Path
1
Define tadbir linguistically and technically
Start with the linguistic root: tadbir comes from 'dubur' meaning 'after' – emancipation after death. Then give the technical definition: attachment of emancipation to the master's absolute death.
The technical definition is the operative one for fiqh.
2
Identify the general conditions of tadbir
Tadbir shares conditions with all emancipations: the master must have legal capacity, the slave must be a valid subject, and the expression must be valid (immediate, conditional, or deferred).
These are general shurut al-'itq.
3
Analyze the specific condition: attachment to absolute death
The emancipation must be attached to the master's death alone, not another's death, and to his absolute death (not restricted by time or description). Example: 'if I die in a hundred years' is considered absolute in meaning.
This distinguishes tadbir from other conditional emancipations.
4
Contrast tadbir with a bequest (wasiyya)
Tadbir is a conditional emancipation, not a bequest. Key difference: tadbir is not revoked by insanity, while a bequest is. Also tadbir is valid under coercion, unlike a bequest.
See the example of insanity: tadbir remains, wasiyya becomes void.
5
Examine the divisibility dispute in co-ownership
Abu Hanifa holds tadbir is divisible; if a co-owner makes tadbir of his share, it applies only to his share. The Sahibayn hold it is not divisible. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
Practical effect: a co-owner can validly make tadbir of his share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التدبير هـ. ما بيان للعتق الواقع بعد الموت بعد ما بين الواقع في الحياة، وقدمه على الاستيلاد لشموله الذكر والأنثى. وله معنيان لغوي وفقهي ؛ فالأول كما في المغرب الإعتاق عن دبر وهو بعد الموت، وتدبر في الأمر نظر في ادباره أي في عواقبه ا وفي ضياء الحلوم: التدبير عتق العبد والأمة بعد الموت وتدبير الأمر النظر فيه إلى ما تصير إليه العاقبة ا هـ . والثاني ما ذكره الشيخ رحمه الله تعالى وركنه اللفظ الدال على معناه وشرائطه نوعان: عام وخاص ؛ فالعام من شرائط العتق فلا يصح إلا من الأهل في المحل منجزاً أو معلقاً أو مضافاً، سواء كان إلى وقت أو إلى الملك أو إلى سببه . والخاص تعليقه بموت المولى فلو علقه بموت غيره لا يكون مدبراً. وأن يكون بمطلق موته وأن يكون بموته وحده كما سيأتي، وأما صفته فالتجزي عنده خلافاً لهما، فلو دبره أحدهما اقتصر على نصيبه وللآخر عند يسار شریکه ست خيارات الخمسة المتقدمة والترك على حاله كما عرف في البدائع. وسيأتي بيان أحكامه من عدم جواز إخراجه عن الملك في حالة الحياة ومن عتقه من الثلث بعد موت المولى إلى آخره قوله : (وهو تعليق العتق بمطلق موته أي موت المولى فخرج بقيد الإطلاق التدبير المقيد كتعليقه بموت موصوف بصفة كما سيأتي وكذا التعليق بموته وموت غيره، وخرج أيضاً أنت حر بعد موتي بيوم أو بشهر فهو وصية بالإعتاق فلا يعتق بعد موت المولى إلا بإعتاق الوارث أو الوصي كما في الذخيرة. وخرج بموته تعليقه بموت غيره كقوله إن مات فلان فأنت حر فإنه لا يصير مديراً أصلاً لا مطلقاً ولا مقيداً، فإذا مات فلان عتق من غير شيء ولا يرد عليه تعليقه بموته إلى مدة لا يعيش مثله إليها كأن مت إلى مائة سنة فأنت ومثله لا يعيش إليها فإنه سيأتي أنه مدبر مطلق على المختار مع أنه لم يعلق عتقه بمطلق موت المولى لأنه وإن كان مقيداً صورة فهو مطلق معنى. وأشار بالتعليق إلى أنه لو دبر عبده ثم ذهب عقله فالتدبير على حاله وإن كان في التدبير معنى الوصية بخلاف ما إذا أوصى برقبته لإنسان ثم جن ثم مات حيث تبطل الوصية والفرق أن التدبير اشتمل على معنى التعليق والتعليق لا يبطل بالجنون ولهذا لا يبطل بالرجوع ولا كذلك الوصية ولهذا جاز تدبير المكره . ولا يجوز وصيته؛ كذا في الظهيرية.
Chapter of Tadbir. It is an explanation of the emancipation that occurs after death, after explaining what occurs during life. He prefaced it over istilad (um walad) because it includes both male and female. It has two meanings: linguistic and technical. The linguistic, as in al-Mughrib, is emancipation after death; and tadabbur in a matter is to consider its consequences. In Diya' al-Hulum: Tadbir is the emancipation of a male or female slave after death, and tadbir of a matter is to consider its outcome. The second is what the Shaykh mentioned (may Allah have mercy on him). Its pillar is the word indicating its meaning, and its conditions are of two types: general and specific. The general are the conditions of emancipation: it is only valid from a legal capacity in a legal subject, whether immediate, conditional, or deferred, whether to a time, to ownership, or to a cause. The specific conditions are: attaching it to the master's death; if attached to another's death, it is not tadbir; it must be to his absolute death; and it must be to his death alone, as will come. As for its attribute: divisibility according to him contrary to them, so if one of two co-owners makes tadbir, it is confined to his share, and the other co-owner, if his partner is wealthy, has the five previously mentioned options and leaving it as is, as known in al-Bada'i. The rulings will come: that it is not permissible to remove it from ownership during life, and that it is freed from the third after the master's death, etc. His saying: (It is the attachment of emancipation to his absolute death) meaning the master's death. So by the restriction of absoluteness, the restricted tadbir is excluded, like attaching it to a death described with a quality, as will come, and similarly attaching it to his death and another's death. Also excluded is 'you are free a day or a month after my death', for that is a bequest of emancipation, so it is not freed after the master's death except by the heir's or executor's emancipation, as in al-Dhakhira. Also excluded by 'his death' is attaching it to another's death, like saying: if so-and-so dies, you are free; then he does not become a mudabbar at all, neither absolute nor restricted. When so-and-so dies, he is freed without anything. And the objection of attaching it to his death to a period he would not live to, like 'if I die in a hundred years, you are free' and he would not live to that, will come that he is an absolute mudabbar according to the chosen opinion, even though he did not attach his emancipation to the absolute death of the master, because although it is restricted in form, it is absolute in meaning. By 'attachment', he indicates that if he made tadbir of his slave and then lost his mind, the tadbir remains, even though tadbir has the meaning of a bequest, unlike if he bequeathed his raqabah to a person and then became insane and then died, where the bequest is void. The difference is that tadbir includes the meaning of attachment, and attachment is not nullified by insanity, so it is not nullified by revocation, unlike a bequest. For this reason, the tadbir of a coerced person is valid, but his bequest is not. Thus in al-Zahiriyya.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage defines tadbir (the act of making a slave a mudabbar) and outlines its conditions. The commentator first explains that the chapter on tadbir comes after the chapter on immediate emancipation because tadbir is a delayed emancipation upon the master's death. He then gives the linguistic meaning of tadbir as 'emancipation after death' and notes that the term is derived from 'dubur' meaning 'back' or 'after'. The technical definition is that it is the attachment of emancipation to the master's absolute death. The pillar (rukn) of tadbir is the verbal expression that indicates this meaning. The conditions are divided into two categories: general conditions (those that apply to any emancipation, such as legal capacity, proper subject, and valid expression whether immediate, conditional, or deferred) and specific conditions (that the emancipation must be attached to the master's death alone, and to his absolute death, not to a specific time or another's death). The passage also discusses the effect of insanity on tadbir as opposed to a bequest: tadbir remains effective even if the master becomes insane, because it is similar to a conditional contract, which is not voided by insanity. It contrasts this with a bequest (wasiyya), which is nullified by the testator's insanity. Finally, it notes that tadbir is valid even if done under coercion, unlike a bequest. The commentary cites al-Zahiriyya for this distinction.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A contract by which a master declares that his slave will be free upon the master's death; it is a conditional emancipation.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free upon the master's death.
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest or will; in this context, a bequest of emancipation of a slave, which is different from tadbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave: 'If I die, you are free, but if my son dies first, you are free,' what is the ruling?
A) The slave becomes a mudabbar upon the master's death.
B) The slave becomes a mudabbar upon the son's death.
C) It is not a valid tadbir because the condition is attached to two different deaths.
D) It is a valid tadbir, but the condition is interpreted as applying to the master's death only.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir is a conditional emancipation that must be attached exclusively to the master's absolute death; it is distinct from a bequest and divisible in co-ownership per Abu Hanifa.

Explicit and Implicit Wordings of Tadbir in Hanafi Law
Enumerates explicit and implicit wordings for tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the explicit and implicit wordings that create a valid tadbir according to the Hanafi school, and explain when intention is required.

Core Idea
Any wording that clearly ties freedom to the master's death creates tadbir, even if implied through custom.

The declaration of tadbir is a form of emancipation that takes effect upon the master's death. Hanafi jurists have detailed the precise wordings—both explicit and metaphorical—that legally establish this contract. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, lists these wordings and clarifies the role of intention and contextual clues. This lesson dissects those wordings and their legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify explicit wordings
List the direct phrases from the passage that unambiguously create tadbir: e.g., 'if I die you are free', 'you are free the day I die', 'from my death', 'I make you tadbir'.
These require no additional intention.
2
Understand the interpretation of 'day'
Note that 'day' in 'you are free the day I die' means absolute time, so freedom occurs regardless of time of death unless the master intends only daytime.
If the master intends only daytime, the tadbir is restricted and the slave may be sold.
3
Recognize synonyms for death
Words like 'incident', 'passing away', 'destruction' are valid if customarily understood as death.
Consideration is to meaning, not literal wording.
4
Analyze implicit wordings (kinayah)
Phrases like 'no one has any way over you after my death' create tadbir even without explicit intention due to the strong contextual clue 'after my death'.
Context can remove the need for intention in kinayah.
5
Distinguish explicit from implicit based on need for intention
Explicit wordings require no intention; implicit ones may require intention unless context suffices.
The passage gives the example of 'free him after my death' as effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (كادامت فأنت حر وأنت حر يوم أموت أو عن دبر مني أو دبرتك) بيان لبعض ألفاظه الصريحة فإنه إثبات العتق عن دبر واليوم هنا لمطلق الوقت فيعتق مات المولى ليلاً أو نهاراً، لأنه قرن بفعل لا يمتد فإن نوى باليوم النهار دون الليل صحت نيته لأنه نوى حقيقة كلامه ثم لا يكون مدبراً لأنه علق عتقه بما ليس بكائن لا محالة وهو موته بالنهار وربما يموت بالليل فلذا لا يكون مدبراً؛ كذا في المبسوط . أي لا يكون مدبراً مطلقاً وإنما هو مقيد فيعتق بموته نهاراً وله بيعه ومثل التعليق بإذا «متى» و «إن» والحدث كالموت فلو قال إن حدث فأنت بي حر فهو مدبر لأنه تعورف الحدث والحادث في الموت، كذا الوفاة والهلاك لأن الاعتبار للمعنى، وكذا أنت حر مع موتي أو في موتي فإنه تعليق العتق بالموت وفي» تستعار بمعنى حرف الشرط كما عرف في الأصول وقول الزيلعي تبعاً لما في المحيط حرف الظرف إذا دخل على الفعل يصير شرطاً تسامح وإنما هو بمعناه لأنه لو كان شرطاً لطلقت في قوله لأجنبية أنت طالق في نكاحك مع أنها لا تطلق. وأفاد بقوله أنت حر يوم أموت أن كل لفظ وقع به العتق للحال إذا أضيف إلى الموت فإنه يوجب التدبير كقوله أعتقتك أو أنت عتيق أو عتق أو محرر بعد موتي. وفي الخانية والظهيرية رجل قال لعبده لا سبيل لأحد عليك بعد موتي قالوا يصير مديراً ا اه. ولم يقيداه بالنية مع أن لا سبيل لي عليك كناية لا يعتق بها إلا بالنية إلا أن يفرق بين قوله لي وبين قوله لأحد، وكذا بعد موتي قرينة لا تتوقف على النية. وفي الحاوي القدسي : لو قال أعتقوه بعد موتي فهو مدبر ا هـ. وقيد بكون السيد واحداً لأنه لو كان بين اثنين فقالا إذا متنا فأنت حر لم يصر بذلك مدبراً ولهما أن يبيعاه، فإذا مات أحدهما صار مدبراً من قبل الثاني وصار حكمه حكم عبد بين رجلين دبره أحدهما. ولو كان كل واحد منهما قال إذا مت فأنت حر أو دبرتك أو دبرت نصيبي منك وخرج القولان منهما جميعاً صار مدبراً بينهما فلا يجوز بيعه وأيهما مات عتق نصيبه وسعى العبد للآخر في قيمة نصيبه منه وكان ولاؤه بينهما ؛ كذا في الحاوي القدسي. ولا فرق في العتق المضاف إلى الموت بين أن يكون معلقاً بشرط آخر أو لا، فلو قال إن كلمت فلاناً فأنت
His saying: (like 'if I die you are free', 'you are free the day I die', 'from my death', or 'I make you tadbir') is an explanation of some explicit wordings. It is the affirmation of emancipation from death, and 'day' here means absolute time, so he is freed whether the master dies at night or during the day, because it is attached to an action that does not extend. If he intended by 'day' the daytime only, his intention is valid because he intended the literal meaning of his speech, then he is not a mudabbar because he attached his emancipation to something not necessarily occurring, which is his death during the day; perhaps he may die at night, so he is not a mudabbar. So in al-Mabsut, he is not an absolute mudabbar but rather restricted; he is freed by death during the day, and the master can sell him. Similar is attachment with 'if', 'when', 'whenever', and 'incident' like death; so if he says 'if an incident occurs, you are free', he is a mudabbar because 'incident' is customarily understood as death, similarly 'passing away' and 'destruction' because consideration is to meaning. Similarly, 'you are free with my death' or 'in my death' is attachment of emancipation to death, and 'in' is used metaphorically as a conditional particle as known in usul. The statement of al-Zayla'i following what is in al-Muhit that 'the particle of time when it enters a verb becomes conditional' is a laxity; rather it is in its meaning, because if it were conditional, then in his statement to a foreign woman 'you are divorced in your marriage' she would be divorced, but she is not. And he informed by his saying 'you are free the day I die' that every word by which instantaneous emancipation occurs, if added to death, creates tadbir, like 'I free you', 'you are free', 'free', or 'liberated after my death'. In al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya: A man said to his slave 'no one has any way over you after my death'; they said he becomes a mudabbar. They did not qualify it with intention, even though 'no way over me' is a metaphor that does not free except with intention, except that there is a difference between his saying 'for me' and his saying 'for anyone', and 'after my death' is a contextual indication that does not require intention. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi: If he said 'free him after my death', he is a mudabbar. He restricted it to the master being one because if there were two, and they said 'when we die, you are free', he does not become a mudabbar by that, and they may sell him. When one of them dies, he becomes a mudabbar from the second, and his ruling becomes like that of a slave between two men when one of them made him tadbir. If each of them said 'when I die, you are free' or 'I make you tadbir' or 'I make my share from you tadbir', and the two statements came from both of them, he becomes a mudabbar between them; he cannot be sold; whichever of them dies, his share is freed, and the slave works for the other for the value of his share, and his wala is between them. Thus in al-Hawi al-Qudsi. There is no difference in emancipation attached to death between being conditional on another condition or not; so if he said 'if you speak to so-and-so, you are free'
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage discusses the various wordings that can be used to create a mudabbar, both explicit and implicit. Explicit phrases include 'if I die you are free', 'you are free the day I die', 'from my back', or 'I make you tadbir'. The phrase 'day' is interpreted as absolute time, so freedom occurs upon death regardless of time of day; however, if the master intends only daytime, his intention is effective, but then the tadbir is restricted: the slave is only freed if death occurs during the day, and the master retains the right to sell him. The passage also clarifies that synonyms for death such as 'incident', 'passing away', 'destruction' are considered valid if customarily understood as death. There is a subtle point about the word 'in' (في) when used in phrases like 'you are free in my death': it is not a conditional particle but is used metaphorically to indicate attachment to death. The passage then discusses implicit wordings: for example, saying 'no one has any way over you after my death' creates tadbir even without explicit intention, because the phrase 'after my death' serves as a clear contextual indication. Similarly, 'free him after my death' is effective. The passage then addresses co-ownership: if two masters jointly say 'when we die, you are free', the slave does not become a mudabbar during their joint lives, and they may sell him. However, if one dies, the slave becomes a mudabbar only from the surviving master, and the ruling is like that of a slave co-owned where one master makes tadbir of his share. If each master individually declares tadbir (e.g., 'when I die, you are free'), then the slave becomes a mudabbar between them, cannot be sold, and upon the death of each, his share is freed, with the slave working to compensate the other for the value of the freed share. The passage concludes by stating that there is no difference between an emancipation attached to death with or without an additional condition (e.g., 'if you speak to so-and-so, you are free' is cut off).

Key Terms
لفظ صريح (lafz sarih): An explicit wording that directly indicates tadbir without need for intention, e.g., 'if I die you are free'.
كناية (kinayah): A metaphorical expression that requires intention to create tadbir, but if clear contextual indications are present, intention may not be necessary.
ولاء (wala): The bond of clientage that arises between the freed slave and the emancipator; it affects inheritance and other rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT an explicit wording for tadbir?
A) You are free the day I die
B) If I die you are free
C) No one has any way over you after my death
D) From my death (dabartuka)

Key Takeaway
Tadbir can be created by both explicit statements and implicit expressions that, through custom, clearly tie freedom to the master's death.

Tadbir in Co-owned Slaves
Explains tadbir rulings for co-owned slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on tadbir when a slave is co-owned, including the effect of joint versus individual declarations and the division of wala.

Core Idea
If co-owners jointly declare tadbir without individualizing, the slave does not become mudabbar; but if each declares individually, the slave becomes mudabbar between them.

When a slave is owned by multiple masters, the rules of tadbir become more complex. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details two key scenarios: joint declaration ('when we die, you are free') and individual declarations ('when I die, you are free'). This lesson unpacks these rulings, including the effect of one owner's death, the prohibition on sale, and the division of clientage (wala).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main co-ownership scenarios
The passage contrasts: (1) both owners jointly say 'when we die, you are free', and (2) each owner individually says 'when I die, you are free'.
The joint declaration does not create tadbir during their joint lives.
2
Understand the ruling for joint declaration
If both say 'when we die', the slave is not a mudabbar; the owners may sell him. However, after one dies, the slave becomes a mudabbar from the surviving owner.
This is a conditional tadbir triggered by the first death.
3
Analyze the ruling for individual declarations
If each individually declares tadbir (e.g., 'when I die, you are free'), the slave becomes a mudabbar between them. He cannot be sold.
Both declarations are independent and cumulative.
4
Determine the effect of one owner's death
When one owner dies, his share is freed. The slave must work (and earn) for the surviving owner to compensate for the value of the freed share.
The slave is not fully freed until the second owner dies.
5
Note the division of wala (clientage)
In individual declarations, the wala (clientage) is divided between the two owners, not solely with the one who dies.
Wala follows the proportional share in the slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (كادامت فأنت حر وأنت حر يوم أموت أو عن دبر مني أو دبرتك) بيان لبعض ألفاظه الصريحة فإنه إثبات العتق عن دبر واليوم هنا لمطلق الوقت فيعتق مات المولى ليلاً أو نهاراً، لأنه قرن بفعل لا يمتد فإن نوى باليوم النهار دون الليل صحت نيته لأنه نوى حقيقة كلامه ثم لا يكون مدبراً لأنه علق عتقه بما ليس بكائن لا محالة وهو موته بالنهار وربما يموت بالليل فلذا لا يكون مدبراً؛ كذا في المبسوط . أي لا يكون مدبراً مطلقاً وإنما هو مقيد فيعتق بموته نهاراً وله بيعه ومثل التعليق بإذا «متى» و «إن» والحدث كالموت فلو قال إن حدث فأنت بي حر فهو مدبر لأنه تعورف الحدث والحادث في الموت، كذا الوفاة والهلاك لأن الاعتبار للمعنى، وكذا أنت حر مع موتي أو في موتي فإنه تعليق العتق بالموت وفي» تستعار بمعنى حرف الشرط كما عرف في الأصول وقول الزيلعي تبعاً لما في المحيط حرف الظرف إذا دخل على الفعل يصير شرطاً تسامح وإنما هو بمعناه لأنه لو كان شرطاً لطلقت في قوله لأجنبية أنت طالق في نكاحك مع أنها لا تطلق. وأفاد بقوله أنت حر يوم أموت أن كل لفظ وقع به العتق للحال إذا أضيف إلى الموت فإنه يوجب التدبير كقوله أعتقتك أو أنت عتيق أو عتق أو محرر بعد موتي. وفي الخانية والظهيرية رجل قال لعبده لا سبيل لأحد عليك بعد موتي قالوا يصير مديراً ا اه. ولم يقيداه بالنية مع أن لا سبيل لي عليك كناية لا يعتق بها إلا بالنية إلا أن يفرق بين قوله لي وبين قوله لأحد، وكذا بعد موتي قرينة لا تتوقف على النية. وفي الحاوي القدسي : لو قال أعتقوه بعد موتي فهو مدبر ا هـ. وقيد بكون السيد واحداً لأنه لو كان بين اثنين فقالا إذا متنا فأنت حر لم يصر بذلك مدبراً ولهما أن يبيعاه، فإذا مات أحدهما صار مدبراً من قبل الثاني وصار حكمه حكم عبد بين رجلين دبره أحدهما. ولو كان كل واحد منهما قال إذا مت فأنت حر أو دبرتك أو دبرت نصيبي منك وخرج القولان منهما جميعاً صار مدبراً بينهما فلا يجوز بيعه وأيهما مات عتق نصيبه وسعى العبد للآخر في قيمة نصيبه منه وكان ولاؤه بينهما ؛ كذا في الحاوي القدسي. ولا فرق في العتق المضاف إلى الموت بين أن يكون معلقاً بشرط آخر أو لا، فلو قال إن كلمت فلاناً فأنت

The Effect of Speech on Tadbir Declarations
States the ruling when a master speaks after declaring tadbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a tadbir becomes absolute through the master's speech, and apply it to conditional tadbir formulations.

Core Idea
Speech confirms a tadbir, making it absolute and binding immediately.

In the Hanafi school, a tadbir (declaration that a slave will be free after the master's death) is a valid legal act. However, this short passage from the Book of Emancipation highlights an important nuance: the master's subsequent speech to the slave can make the tadbir absolute. Similarly, if the tadbir is conditioned on the slave speaking to a third party, the fulfilment of that condition activates the tadbir. This lesson unpacks these two scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the first case: master says 'free after my death' and then speaks to the slave. The ruling is that the slave becomes mudabbar. Note the reason: the speaking makes the tadbir absolute.
'Mudabbar' means a slave whose freedom is postponed until the master's death.
2
Understand the conditional scenario
The second case involves a condition: 'you are free after you speak to so-and-so and after my death.' When the slave speaks to that person, he becomes mudabbar. This shows that a contingent tadbir becomes effective upon fulfilment of the condition.
The condition is the slave's speech, not the master's.
3
Extract the underlying principle
The common principle is that speech (or an act) that confirms the intention behind the tadbir solidifies it and makes it binding. Without such confirmation, the tadbir may remain revocable or incomplete.
This principle is consistent with the Hanafi approach to conditional declarations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتق باب التدبير
حر بعد موتي فكلمه صار مديراً لأنه بعد الكلام صار التدبير مطلقاً، وكذا لو قال أنت حر بعد كلامك فلاناً وبعد موتي فكلمه فلان كان مديراً ; كذا في البدائع.
Book of Emancipation, Chapter of Tadbir. [If one says] 'free after my death' and then speaks to him, he becomes mudabbar because after speaking the tadbir became absolute. Similarly if he said 'you are free after you speak to so-and-so and after my death,' and he spoke to him, he becomes mudabbar; thus in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the effect of speech in tadbir. The author states that if a master says to his slave 'you are free after my death' and then immediately speaks to him (i.e., addresses him), the slave becomes a mudabbar. The reason given is that the speech makes the previously general tadbir absolute, as it confirms the master's intent. Similarly, if the master says 'you are free after you speak to so-and-so and after my death,' and the slave then speaks to that person, he becomes mudabbar at that moment. This is cited from al-Bada'i. The key point is that the act of speaking removes any ambiguity and establishes the tadbir immediately.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free after the master's death.
تدبير (tadbir): The act of declaring a slave to be free after the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a master says to his slave 'you are free after my death' and then immediately speaks to him?
A) The slave does not become mudabbar until the master dies.
B) The slave becomes mudabbar immediately because the speech makes the tadbir absolute.
C) The tadbir is nullified because the master spoke.
D) The slave is freed immediately.

Key Takeaway
Speech after a tadbir declaration makes the tadbir absolute and the slave becomes mudabbar immediately, regardless of whether the speech is by the master or the fulfilment of a condition by the slave.

Conditional Tadbir: The Role of the Master's Intention
Explains conditional tadbir and the master's prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of the master's intention and the slave's wish in a conditional tadbir, and determine when the slave becomes mudabbar.

Core Idea
The validity of a conditional tadbir hinges on the master's intention regarding when the slave's wish must occur.

Take the case of a master who tells his slave, 'You will be free after I die if you wish.' Does this create a valid tadbir? It depends entirely on what the master meant by 'if you wish' — was it immediate or after death? In this lesson, we unpack Imam Muhammad's ruling from al-Asl, which clarifies this subtle but critical distinction. We also examine the master's right to prohibit the slave from wishing, and the equivalence of immediate and deferred tadbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations of 'in shi'ta'
The master may intend the slave's wish to occur immediately (al-sa'a) or after death (ba'd al-mawt). The meaning of 'if you wish' is ambiguous and must be clarified by the master's intention.
This distinction is crucial because it determines when the slave can validly wish.
2
Determine the consequence of each interpretation
If the master intends immediate wish, the slave becomes mudabbar by wishing at that very moment. If he intends after-death wish, the slave may only wish after the master's death, and then becomes free from one-third of the estate.
The comparison to 'if you enter the house' shows that a condition (shart) triggers the tadbir when fulfilled.
3
Analyze the master's prohibition
The master may validly prohibit the slave from wishing before death. This prohibition is effective and prevents the slave from forming a valid wish.
The master retains full authority over the slave's actions.
4
Extend the rule to deferred tadbir
There is no difference between an immediate tadbir declaration and a deferred one (e.g., 'you are mudabbar tomorrow'). When the specified time arrives, the slave becomes mudabbar without needing a new declaration.
Deferred tadbir is treated as effective from the moment of declaration, with effect postponed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر محمد في الأصل إذا قال أنت حر بعد موتي إن شئت فإن نوى بقوله إن شئت الساعة فشاء العبد في ساعته تلك صار مديراً لأنه علق التدبير بشرط وهو المشيئة وقد وجد كما إذا قال إن دخلت الدار فأنت مدبر، وإن عنی به مشيئته بعد الموت فليس للعبد مشيئة حتى يموت المولى فإن مات المولى فشاء بعد موته فهو حر من ثلثه. وذكر الحاكم في مختصره أن المراد منه أ أن يعتقه الوصي أو الوارث. وفي المحيط : ولو نهاه عن المشيئة قبل موته جاز نهيه ولا فرق في التدبير بين أن يكون منجزاً أو مضافاً كما إذا قال أنت مدبر غداً أو رأس شهر كذا فإذا جاء الوقت صار مدبراً.
Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl: If he says 'you are free after my death if you wish,' and he intended by 'if you wish' the immediate moment, and the slave wishes in that same moment, he becomes mudabbar because he conditioned tadbir on a condition, which is the wish, and it has occurred, just as if he said 'if you enter the house, you are mudabbar.' If he intended by it his wish after death, then the slave has no wish until the master dies; then if the master dies and he wishes after his death, he is free from one-third of his estate. Al-Hakim mentioned in his Mukhtasar that the meaning of it is that the executor or heir should free him. In al-Muhit: If he prohibited him from wishing before his death, his prohibition is valid. And there is no difference in tadbir between it being immediate or deferred, such as if he said 'you are mudabbar tomorrow' or 'the beginning of such a month,' then when the time comes, he becomes mudabbar.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the conditional tadbir. Imam Muhammad reports in al-Asl that if the master says 'you are free after my death if you wish' and he intends the wish to be immediate, then if the slave wishes at that very moment, he becomes mudabbar. This is because the condition (the slave's wish) is fulfilled. If the master intends the wish to occur after death, then the slave cannot wish until after the master's death, and if he wishes then, he is freed from one-third of the estate (since it is a wasiyya). Al-Hakim interprets that the slave's wish after death is actually the executor or heir freeing him. In al-Muhit, it is stated that the master can validly prohibit the slave from wishing before his death. Finally, the passage clarifies that there is no difference in tadbir between an immediate declaration and one deferred to a specific future time; when that time arrives, the slave becomes mudabbar.

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashī'a): The wish or will of the slave as a condition for tadbir.
مضاف (muḍāf): A deferred tadbir, e.g., 'you are mudabbar tomorrow'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave 'you are free after my death if you wish' intending immediate wish, what is the ruling?
A) The slave becomes mudabbar only if he wishes after the master's death.
B) The slave must be freed immediately.
C) The slave becomes mudabbar if he wishes in that same moment.
D) The tadbir is invalid because it is conditional.

Key Takeaway
In conditional tadbir, the master's intention determines when the slave's wish must occur, and his prohibition is valid; deferred tadbir is equivalent to immediate.

Immediate Tadbir and Conditional Distinctions
Riwaya on immediate tadbir and condition distinctions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that tadbir with the phrase 'after my death' is immediate, and distinguish between valid conditions (wish) and invalid conditions (legatee's action) in tadbir.

Core Idea
Saying 'after my death' is void, making tadbir immediate; conditions on legatee's action void, but condition on beneficiary's wish valid.

This lesson examines a riwaya from Hisham ibn Amr from Imam Muhammad regarding the wording of tadbir. A key Hanafi principle emerges: if a master says 'you are mudabbar after my death,' the declaration takes effect immediately because the phrase 'after my death' is legally void. The passage then distinguishes between valid and invalid conditions that can be attached to tadbir, illustrating the scope of tadbir as a kind of will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the ruling from Hisham's narration: when a master says 'you are mudabbar after my death,' the slave becomes mudabbar immediately (at the moment of utterance). This is because tadbir after death is impossible, so the temporal phrase is void.
2
Understand the voiding mechanism
The phrase 'after my death' is void (yulgha) because tadbir logically cannot take effect after death. The remaining declaration 'you are mudabbar' is interpreted as a declaration of freedom conditional on death, which is the essence of tadbir.
This is based on the principle that the impossible condition is void, leaving the original intent.
3
Distinguish valid vs invalid conditions
Contrast two cases from al-Dhakhira: (a) 'You are free after my death if you enter the house' is invalid because a will cannot be conditioned on the legatee's action. (b) 'You are free after my death if you wish' is valid because attaching a will to the beneficiary's wish is allowed.
The key is whether the condition is on the legatee's own act (invalid) or on their choice (valid).
4
Apply to the umm walad case
Analyze the case from al-Muhit: a man says to an umm walad 'if I own you, you are free after my death' and she gives birth before he buys her. When he buys both mother and child, only the mother becomes mudabbar. The child was born before ownership, so the condition of ownership attaches only to the mother, not the child.
This parallels the rule that a child born before the conditional sale does not benefit from the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروی هشام عن محمد رحمه الله تعالى فيمن قال أنت مدبر بعد موتي فهو مدبر الساعة لأنه أضاف التدبير إلى ما بعد الموت والتدبير بعد الموت لا يتصور فيلغو قوله بعد موتي فيبقى قوله أنت مدبر أي أنت حر فيصير كأنه قال أنت بعد موتي. وفي الذخيرة معزياً إلى الأصل: لو قال أنت حر بعد موتي إن دخلت الدار لا هذا التصرف عندنا أصلاً بخلاف ما إذا قال أنت حر بعد موتي إن شئت. والفرق أن في فصل المشيئة صححنا تصرفه بطريق الوصية وتعليق الوصية بالمشيئة صحيح وتعذر هذا التصرف بطريق الوصية لأن تعليق الوصية بدخول الموصى له الدار باطل وفي المحيط : لو قال لأمة إن ملكتك فأنت حرة بعد موتي فولدت فاشتراهما تصير الأم مدبرة دون الولد لأن التدبير ثبت في الأم والولد منفصل عنها قبل الملك فلا يتصور سراية حق التدبير إلى الولد كما لو قال إن ملكتك فأنت حرة فملكها عتقت ولا يعتق ولد ولدته قبل الملك فكذا هذا ولو قال المولى ولدت قبل التدبير وقالت بل بعده فالقول للمولى مع يمينه على علمه والبينة لها ا هـ . وفي الظهيرية : أنت حر الساعة بعد موتي يعتق
Hisham narrated from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, regarding one who said 'you are mudabbar after my death': he is mudabbar immediately, because he added tadbir to after death, and tadbir after death is inconceivable, so his saying 'after my death' becomes void, leaving his saying 'you are mudabbar' meaning 'you are free,' so it becomes as if he said 'you are free after my death.' In al-Dhakhira, attributed to al-Asl: If he said 'you are free after my death if you enter the house,' this disposition is not valid with us at all, unlike if he said 'you are free after my death if you wish.' The difference is that in the case of wish we validate his disposition by way of a will (wasiyya), and attaching a will to a wish is valid, but this disposition is impossible by way of a will because attaching a will to the legatee's entering the house is invalid. In al-Muhit: If he said to an umm walad 'if I own you, then you are free after my death,' and she gave birth, then he bought both, the mother becomes mudabbar but not the child, because tadbir was established in the mother and the child was separated from her before ownership, so the right of tadbir does not extend to the child, just as if he said 'if I own you, you are free' and he owned her, she becomes free but not a child born before ownership. Similarly here. If the master said 'you gave birth before tadbir' and she said 'after,' the master's word is taken with his oath on his knowledge, and she has the evidence. In al-Zahiriyya: 'you are free this moment after my death' he is free.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage presents a narration from Hisham ibn Amr about a ruling of Imam Muhammad. If a master says 'you are mudabbar after my death,' the slave becomes mudabbar immediately (i.e., at the moment of utterance). The reason: tadbir after death is impossible, so the phrase 'after my death' is void, leaving the declaration 'you are mudabbar' which is equivalent to 'you are free' conditional on death. This is a key Hanafi principle. Then a distinction is drawn from al-Dhakhira: if he says 'you are free after my death if you enter the house,' this is invalid because a will cannot be conditioned on the legatee's action. However, if he says 'if you wish,' it is valid because a will can be conditioned on the beneficiary's wish. Finally, a case from al-Muhit about an umm walad: if a man says to a slave woman who is not yet owned by him 'if I own you, you are free after my death,' and she gives birth before he buys her, and then he buys both mother and child, the mother becomes mudabbar but not the child. The child was born before ownership, so the condition of ownership applies only to the mother. If there is a dispute about whether the child was born before or after the tadbir, the master's word is taken with his oath.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child to her master.
وصية (wasiyya): A will or bequest; tadbir is considered a type of wasiyya.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death via tadbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens when a master says 'you are mudabbar after my death'?
A) The slave becomes free immediately.
B) The slave becomes mudabbar immediately.
C) The declaration is invalid.
D) The slave becomes free only after the master dies.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir with 'after my death' is immediate; conditions on the legatee's action invalidate, but conditions on the beneficiary's wish are valid.

Selling a Mudabbar and the Effect of a Judge's Ruling
Explains the ruling on selling a mudabbar and the effect of a judge's ruling allowing it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on selling a mudabbar and evaluate the effect of a judge's ruling on the tadbir, distinguishing between binding (luzum) and conditional (ta'liq) aspects.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling revokes the binding nature of tadbir, not the conditional chance.

This passage examines a nuanced inter-madhhab dispute regarding the sale of a mudabbar—a slave whose freedom is conditional upon the master's death. The Hanafi school generally holds that a mudabbar cannot be sold, but a Shafi'i judge might permit it. The author explores the implications of such a ruling, distinguishing between the binding nature of tadbir (luzum) and the underlying conditional clause. Legal devices (hiyal) are also presented to allow sale under specific wording.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on selling a mudabbar
Identify the default Hanafi position: a mudabbar cannot be sold; any sale is void (batil). Note that this is contested by the Shafi'i school.
The passage begins by referencing this foundational ruling.
2
Analyze the effect of a Shafi'i judge's ruling
If a Shafi'i judge rules the sale valid, the Hanafi school considers this a revocation (faskh) of the tadbir, but only of its binding nature, not the conditional suspension.
The text warns that the tadbir is not completely nullified.
3
Examine the distinction between luzum and ta'liq
The author argues that the dispute is over binding (luzum), not the validity of the conditional suspension (sihhat al-ta'liq). Thus, only the binding is removed by the judge's ruling.
This is the core analytical move in the passage.
4
Consider the legal device (hila) for restricted tadbir
The passage cites legal devices allowing a master to retain the right to sell by wording tadbir as 'if I die and you are in my ownership.' This creates a restricted tadbir that permits sale.
Al-Walwalji and Kitab al-Hiyal provide the examples.
5
Understand the practical consequence
If the slave is sold and later returns to the master, he is not freed upon the master's death because the tadbir was already revoked (binding aspect). Only if he remains in ownership at death does the freedom occur.
This shows the importance of the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متفقاً عليه ولم بجواز بيعه نفذ قضاؤه ويكون ذلك فسخاً للتدبير حتى لو عاد إليه يوماً من الدهر بوجه من الوجوه ثم مات لا يعتق وهذا مشكل، لأنه يبطل بقضاء القاضي ما هو مختلف فيه وما هو مختلف فيه لزوم التدبير لا صحة التعليق فينبغي أن يبطل وصف اللزوم لا غير ا هـ . وسيأتي في البيوع أن بيع المدبر باطل لا يملك بالقبض فلو باعه المولى فرفعه العبد إلى قاض حنفي وادعى عليه أو على المشتري فحكم الحنفي ببطلان البيع ولزوم التدبير فإنه يصير فليس للشافعي أن يقضي بجواز بيعه بعده كما في فتاوى الشيخ قاسم وهو موافق للقواعد فينبغي أن يكون كالحر ، فلو جمع بينه وبين من ينبغي أن يسري الفساد إلى القن كما سنبينه إن شاء الله تعالى في محله . وفي الولوالجية من التدبير : رجل قال هذه أمتي إن احتجت إلى بيعها أبيعها وإن بقيت بعد موتي فهي حرة فباعها جاز ؛ كذا في فتاوى الصدر الشهيد ا هـ . بأنها مدبرة تدبيراً مطلقاً أو مقيداً. وفيها من كتاب الحيل : لو أراد أن يدبر عبده على يصرح وجه يملك بيعه يقول إذا مت وأنت في ملكي فأنت حر فهذا يكون مدبراً مقيداً فيملك بيعه فإذا مات وهو في ملكه عتق ا هـ . فكذا في المسألة الأولى يكون مدبراً مقيداً لكن ذكر الولوالجي رحمه الله في آخر الوصايا : لو قال لعبده إن مت وأنت في ملكي فأنت فله أن حر لأنه لما مات لم يبق في ملكه فلم يعتق ا هـ . وهو ليس بمخالف لقوله في الحيل إنه يعتق بموته لأن قوله في الوصايا لا يعتق معناه لو مات بعد بيعه، وأما لو مات وهو في ملكه فإنه يعتق.
Unanimously agreed upon, and not with the permissibility of selling it, his ruling is executed and that is a revocation of the tadbir, so that if it returns to him someday in any way and then dies, it is not freed. This is problematic, because by the judge's ruling he invalidates what is disputed, and what is disputed is the binding nature of tadbir, not the validity of the conditional suspension. So it should invalidate the attribute of binding only, not otherwise. And it will come in the chapter of sales that the sale of a mudabbar is void, not owned by taking possession. So if the master sells him, and the slave raises it to a Hanafi judge and claims against him or against the buyer, and the Hanafi judge rules the sale void and the tadbir binding, then it becomes such that the Shafi'i judge cannot rule its sale permissible afterwards, as in the fatwas of Shaykh Qasim, and it is in accordance with the rules, so it should be like a free person. If he combines it with something else, the corruption should extend to the qinn as we will clarify, Allah willing, in its place. And in al-Walwaljiyya from tadbir: A man said, 'This female slave of mine, if I need to sell her I sell her, and if she remains after my death she is free,' so he sold her; it is permissible; thus in the fatwas of al-Sadr al-Shahid. That she is a mudabbara with absolute or restricted tadbir. And in it from Kitab al-Hiyal: If he wants to make his slave mudabbar in a way that he can sell him, he says, 'If I die and you are in my ownership, you are free,' then this is a restricted mudabbar, so he can sell him, and if he dies while in his ownership, he is freed. Similarly, in the first case, he is a restricted mudabbar. But al-Walwalji mentioned at the end of al-Wasaya: If he said to his slave, 'If I die and you are in my ownership, you are free,' he does not become free because when he died, he was not in his ownership, so he is not freed. And this is not contradictory to his statement in al-Hiyal that he is freed upon his death, because his statement in al-Wasaya that he is not freed means if he dies after selling him. But if he dies while in his ownership, he is freed.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the effect of a judge's ruling on the sale of a mudabbar. The Hanafi position is that a mudabbar cannot be sold, and if a judge (especially a Hanafi one) rules the sale void, the tadbir remains binding. However, if a Shafi'i judge allows the sale, the Hanafi view is that this ruling effectively revokes the tadbir (فسخ التدبير), but only the binding nature, not the underlying conditional chance. The text then discusses a problematic scenario: if the mudabbar later returns to the master by any means and then dies, he is not freed because the tadbir was already revoked. The author justifies this by distinguishing between the binding nature and the validity of the conditional clause. The text then provides a legal device (hila) from al-Walwalji and Kitab al-Hiyal: by wording the tadbir as 'if I die and you are in my ownership,' the master retains the right to sell, and only if the slave is still in his ownership at death does freedom occur. This is a restricted tadbir that allows sale. Finally, there is a clarification that al-Walwalji's statement in al-Wasaya does not contradict the hila, as it refers to a case where the slave was sold before death.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A contract by which a master declares his slave free upon the master's death, considered a will (وصية).
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been given tadbir; his freedom is conditional upon the master's death.
فسخ التدبير (faskh al-tadbir): Revocation of the tadbir contract, which effects its binding nature but not necessarily the underlying conditional clause.
لزوم (luzum): Binding nature of a contract or commitment.
تعليق (ta'liq): Conditional suspension; the legal effect is contingent on a future event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of a Hanafi judge's ruling that the sale of a mudabbar is void?
A) The tadbir is completely nullified, and the slave becomes free.
B) The tadbir remains fully binding, and the sale is invalid.
C) The binding nature (luzum) is revoked, but the conditional suspension remains.
D) The judge's ruling has no effect on the tadbir.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the binding nature (luzum) and the conditional suspension (ta'liq) of tadbir; a judge's ruling can affect only the former, allowing legal devices that preserve the master's right to sell.

Emancipation of a Jointly-Owned Mudabbar
Ruling on jointly-owned mudabbar and payment for share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the emancipation of a jointly-owned mudabbar when one partner pays the value, and explain why the wala' remains shared.

Core Idea
Paying the value of a share in a mudabbar does not transfer ownership; the mudabbar becomes free by his own action, so wala' stays shared.

The mudabbar is a slave promised freedom upon the master's death. What happens when two partners jointly own a mudabbar and one partner frees his share by paying the other? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling: the mudabbar is freed, but the wala' remains with both partners. The reasoning is subtle but essential for understanding the Hanafi position on emancipation and ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case
Recognize the scenario: a mudabbar jointly owned by two partners. One partner, being wealthy, frees his share by guaranteeing the value of the other's share.
The mudabbar is a slave whose emancipation is deferred to the master's death (tadbir).
2
State the Ruling
The mudabbar becomes free immediately, and the wala' (clientage) remains shared between both partners as before.
Wala' is the bond of loyalty that entitles the manumitter to inherit from the freed slave.
3
Understand the Reasoning (Talil)
The emancipation is attributed to the mudabbar himself, not to the paying partner, because paying the value does not transfer ownership of the share. The mudabbar, by his own right, effects his freedom after the obstacle (the partner's claim) is removed.
A mudabbar cannot be transferred in ownership; the payment only removes the impediment.
4
Apply the Concept of Wala'
Since the mudabbar is the actual manumitter, the wala' remains with both original owners jointly, just as it was before the payment.
The partner who paid does not gain exclusive wala'.
5
Note an Edge Case
The passage mentions that if the mudabbar is sold together with a qinn (ordinary slave) in one transaction, the corruption affects the entire sale, implying the mudabbar's status impacts the contract.
This is an expansion probe: the author hints at further implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف بعدم جواز تمليكه إلى أنه لو كان المدبر بين اثنين أعتقه أحدهما وهو موسر وضمن قيمة نصيب شريكه عتق المدبر ولم يتغير الولاء لأن العتق ها هنا ثبت من جهة المدبر في الحقيقة لا من جهة الذي أعتقه لأن المعتق بأداء الضمان لا يملك نصيب الشريك ها هنا لأن المدبر لا يقبل الانتقال ملك من إلى ملك، وإنما وجب لإثبات الحيلولة بين المدبر والمولى أما أن يقال إن المعتق يتملك نصيب صاحبه من المدبر فلا . ولما كان هذا طريق العتق كان المعتق هو المدبر فلذا كان الولاء لهما على الشركة كما كان أولاً؛ كذا في الذخيرة ولا يرد عليه أن يقبل الانتقال بالقضاء لأنه بالقضاء ينفسخ التدبير، وأما ها هنا فالتدبير باق ولكن كان ينبغي أنه لو ضم إلى قن وبيعا صفقة واحدة أن الفساد إلى القن كالحر وسيتضح في محله إن شاء الله تعالى.
And the author indicated by the impermissibility of transferring ownership to him that if the mudabbar is between two people, and one of them frees him while he is wealthy and guarantees the value of his partner's share, the mudabbar is freed and the wala' does not change, because the emancipation here is established from the side of the mudabbar in reality, not from the side of the one who freed him, because the one who frees by paying the guarantee does not own the partner's share here, since the mudabbar does not accept transfer of ownership from one to another. It is only obligated to establish a separation between the mudabbar and the master. As for saying that the manumitter becomes the owner of his companion's share from the mudabbar, no. And since this is the way of emancipation, the manumitter is the mudabbar, so the wala' is for both jointly as it was initially; thus in al-Dhakhira. And it is not refuted by the fact that he accepts transfer by judicial ruling, because by judicial ruling the tadbir is annulled. Here the tadbir remains, but it would be appropriate that if he is combined with a qinn and sold in one lot, the corruption extends to the qinn as free, and it will become clear in its place, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Marghinani's al-Hidayah commentary regarding a mudabbar owned by two partners. If one partner frees his share by paying the value of the other's share (because he is wealthy and guarantees it), the mudabbar becomes free, but the wala' (loyalty) remains shared between both partners. The reasoning is that the emancipation is actually from the mudabbar himself, not from the manumitting partner, because the partner does not own the share of the other – the mudabbar cannot be transferred in ownership. The payment is only to remove the obstacle (the partner's claim). Therefore, the mudabbar is considered the effective manumitter, and the wala' stays as it was. The passage also mentions that if the mudabbar is sold together with a qinn slave in one transaction, the corruption of the sale affects the qinn as well, implying that the mudabbar's status causes the entire sale to be invalid.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose manumission is deferred to the death of his master (tadbir).
ولاء (wala'): The relationship of loyalty between the freed slave and the manumitter, by virtue of which the manumitter inherits the slave.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; here, the payment made by one partner to the other for the value of the share in the mudabbar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a mudabbar owned by two partners, if one partner frees his share by paying the value, what happens to the wala'?
A) The wala' goes exclusively to the paying partner.
B) The wala' is divided between the partners in proportion to their shares.
C) The wala' remains shared as it was before.
D) The wala' is nullified.

Key Takeaway
When one partner pays the value of his share in a mudabbar, the mudabbar becomes free, but the wala' remains jointly with both partners.

Rights of the Owner Over the Mudabbar and Mudabbara
States master's permissive rights over mudabbar/mudabbara.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permitted actions of a master over a mudabbar/mudabbara and explain why ownership remains the basis.

Core Idea
Ownership of the mudabbar continues, so the master may use, hire, marry off, and have intercourse.

The mudabbar is a slave promised freedom upon the master's death. Does this promise restrict the master's rights? The Hanafi school clarifies: ownership remains fully intact until death, so all normal owner actions are permitted as long as they don't annul the tadbir. This lesson examines the passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq that affirms these rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The passage discusses male (mudabbar) and female (mudabbara) slaves with tadbir. Recognize that they are still slaves under ownership.
Mudabbar/mudabbara are not free yet; tadbir is a promise of future freedom.
2
List the permitted actions
The text explicitly mentions four actions: استخدام (using/hiring out), إجارة (hiring out), وطء (intercourse for female), and نكاح (marrying off). Note that marriage may be forced (جبراً).
For the male mudabbar, the only actions are using and hiring; marriage is also allowed but not stated here explicitly for male (implied by 'كذا المدبر').
3
Understand the legal basis
The basis is that ownership (ملك) remains in the master. Ownership grants the authority (ولاية) to perform these actions.
Without ownership, such authority would not exist.
4
Apply the criterion from al-Dhakhira
The criterion: any action that is permissible with a free person is also permissible with a mudabbar, provided it does not invalidate the tadbir (the reason for the contract).
This explains why selling is not mentioned – selling would invalidate tadbir.
5
Recognize the consequences
Because the mudabbar remains property, all earnings (kasb), blood-money (arsh), and dowry (mahr) belong to the master.
This is a direct consequence of continued ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويستخدم ويؤجر وتوطأ وتنكح أي ويستخدم المدبر ويؤجر وكذا المدبرة وتوطأ المدبرة أي يجوز للمولى ذلك ويجوز أن يزوجها جبراً عليها وكذا المدبر كما تقدم في نكاح الرقيق. وإنما جازت هذه التصرفات لأن الملك ثابت فيه وبه تستفاد ولاية هذه التصرفات . وضابطها كما في الذخيرة أن كل تصرف يقع في الحر فإنه لا يمنع في المدبر والمدبرة لأنه لا يبطل ما انعقد له من السبب. وأفاد المصنف رحمه الله بجواز ذلك أن أكساب المدبر والمدبرة للمولى وكذا أرشهما وكذا مهرها للمولى لأنهما بقيا على حكم ملك المولى؛ كذا في الذخيرة.
His saying: (And he is used, and hired, and she is had intercourse with, and married) meaning the mudabbar is used and hired, and likewise the mudabbara, and the mudabbara is had intercourse with, i.e., it is permissible for the master to do that, and it is permissible to marry her off by force, and likewise the mudabbar, as previously mentioned in the marriage of slaves. These actions are only permissible because ownership is established in him, and by it (the owner) derives authority for these actions. The criterion, as in al-Dhakhira, is that every action that occurs with a free person is not prevented regarding the mudabbar and mudabbara, because it does not invalidate the reason for which they were contracted. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated that by allowing that, the earnings of the mudabbar and mudabbara go to the master, and likewise their blood-money, and likewise her dowry goes to the master, because they remain under the rule of the master's ownership; thus in al-Dhakhira.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It explains that a mudabbar (male slave promised freedom upon master's death) and a mudabbara (female) can be used by the master for service, hired out, and the master can have intercourse with the female mudabbara and marry her off (including forced marriage). The same applies to the male mudabbar regarding marriage. The justification is that the master retains ownership over the mudabbar, and ownership gives authority for such actions. The criterion is that any act that is permissible with a free person (like marriage, hiring) does not invalidate the tadbir, so it is allowed. The master also takes all earnings (kasb), blood-money (arsh), and dowry (mahr) of the mudabbar/a because they remain his property.

Key Terms
مدبرة (mudabbara): Female slave who has been given tadbir; she is promised freedom upon master's death.
أرش (arsh): Blood-money or compensation paid for injury to the slave; goes to the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, is it permissible for the master to have intercourse with the female mudabbara?
A) Yes, because ownership remains.
B) No, because it would prevent her freedom.
C) Only if she consents.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The master retains full ownership of the mudabbar/mudabbara, so all owner actions are permissible as long as they do not invalidate the tadbir.
