Rulings on the Mudabbar: Debts, Crimes, and Offspring
Rulings on debt, crime, and offspring of the mudabbar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the mudabbar's debts, crimes against the master, and the status of his offspring.

Core Idea
The mudabbar's person is protected from sale for debt; his crimes against the master are limited to the lesser of value or blood-money.

This passage from al-Hidayah (via al-Bahr al-Raiq) summarizes several key rulings concerning the mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death). The Hanafi school protects his person from sale for debt, attaches debts to his earnings, and sets special rules for crimes against the master and the status of his offspring. Understanding these rules is essential for grasping the unique legal personality of the mudabbar.

Guided Path
1
Debt Attachment
State the ruling: the mudabbar's debts are not attached to his person (raqaba) because it cannot be sold; instead they are attached to his earnings, and he must work to pay them.
This protects the mudabbar from being sold to pay debts, preserving the promise of freedom.
2
Crime Against Master
If the mudabbar commits a crime against the master, the liability is the lesser of the mudabbar's value or the blood-money of the crime. The master is not liable for more than one value even if multiple crimes occur.
This limits the master's recovery and protects the mudabbar's potential freedom.
3
Offspring Status
The child of a mudabbara (female mudabbar) takes her status. If the tadbir was absolute, the child becomes free upon the master's death along with the mother. If the tadbir was restricted (e.g., conditional), the child is not mudabbar.
Note the correction: the following is based on the mother, not the father, as stated in some copies of al-Hidayah.
4
Tadbir of Fetus
Tadbir of a fetus alone is permissible, like emancipating it. If the mother gives birth in less than six months from the tadbir, the child is mudabbar; otherwise not.
This relies on the presumption that a child born within six months is the same as the fetus at the time of tadbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكامه أن ومن دینه لا يتعلق برقبته لأنها لا تحتمل البيع ويتعلق بكسبه ويسعى في ديونه بالغة ما بلغت . ومنها أن جنايته على المولى وهو الأقل من قيمته ومن أرش الجناية ولا يضمن المولى أكثر من قيمة واحدة وإن كثرت الجنايات على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. وولد المدبرة بمنزلتها كالحرة فيعتق بموت سيد أمه إن كان التدبير مطلقاً، أما ولد المدبرة تدبيراً مقيداً فلا يكون مدبراً. ووقع في بعض نسخ الهداية أن ولد المدبر بالتذكير وليس بصحيح لأن التبعية إنما هي للأم لا للأب وتدبير الحمل وحده جائز كعتقه فإن ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر كان مديراً وإلا فلا
Among its rulings: his debt is not attached to his person because it cannot be sold, and it is attached to his earnings, and he works to pay his debts however much they are. And among them: his crime against the master is the lesser of his value and the blood-money of the crime, and the master is not liable for more than one value even if many crimes, as will come, Allah willing. And the child of the mudabbara is in her status like a free person, so he becomes free upon the death of his mother's master if the tadbir was absolute. As for the child of a mudabbara with restricted tadbir, he is not mudabbar. And it appears in some copies of al-Hidayah that the child of the mudabbar is masculine, but it is not correct because the following is only for the mother, not the father. And tadbir of the fetus alone is permissible like its emancipation; if she gives birth in less than six months, it is mudabbar, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage outlines several rulings regarding the mudabbar. First, the mudabbar's debts are not attached to his person (raqaba) because it cannot be sold to pay them; instead, they are attached to his earnings, and he is required to work to pay off his debts. Second, if the mudabbar commits a crime against the master, the liability is the lesser of the mudabbar's value or the blood-money, and the master is not liable for more than one value even if multiple crimes occur. Third, the child of a mudabbara takes her status: if the mother's tadbir was absolute, the child becomes free upon the master's death along with the mother. If the tadbir was restricted (e.g., conditional on the master's ownership at death), the child is not mudabbar. The text also corrects a copy error in al-Hidayah that said 'child of the mudabbar' (masculine), emphasizing that the following is based on the mother. Finally, tadbir of a fetus alone is permissible, like emancipating it; if born before six months, the tadbir applies, otherwise not.

Key Terms
رقبة (raqaba): The person of the slave; here, debts are not attached to it because it cannot be sold.
جناية المدبر على المولى (jinayat al-mudabbar 'ala al-mawla): Crime committed by the mudabbar against the master, the liability is the lesser of value or blood-money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mudabbara with absolute tadbir gives birth to a child, what is the status of the child upon the master's death?
A) The child is free along with the mother.
B) The child is not free unless separately declared.
C) The child becomes the master's property.
D) The child must serve the master's heirs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely protects the mudabbar's person from sale for debt, and his crimes against the master are limited to the lesser of value or blood-money.

The Mudabbar Freed from One-Third: Ruling and Proof
Establishes the basic rule and proof for tadbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tadbir, explain the hadith proof, and identify the cross-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Tadbir is a will — thus the mudabbar is freed only from one-third, not the whole estate.

This passage establishes the fundamental ruling that tadbir is like a will, hence freedom is limited to one-third of the master's wealth. The Prophet's hadith 'He is free from the third' provides direct proof, and the analogy to a will reinforces the limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is tadbir (a declaration that a slave will be free after the master's death). The ruling: upon death, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's estate.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the hadith 'He is free from the third' and the reasoning that tadbir is a will (wasiyya).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'min al-thuluth' (from the third) directly limits freedom to one-third. The analogy to a will strengthens this: since a will is executed from one-third, tadbir is treated similarly.
Hanafi usul: al-amm yufidu al-wujub? Here the hadith is specific.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may not treat tadbir as a will, or may allow freedom from the entire estate. The Hanafi position is that it is like a will and thus limited.
Cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) based on the hadith and the principle that tadbir is a donation conditioned on death.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبموته يعتق من ثلثه أي بموت المولى يعتق المدبر من ثلث مال المولى لما روينا من قوله عليه السلام وهو حر من الثلث ولأن التدبير وصية لأنه تبرع مضاف إلى وقت الموت والحكم غير ثابت في الحال فينفذ من الثلث، ولكونه وصية حتى لو قتله المدبر فإنه يسعى في جميع قيمته لأنه لا وصية للقاتل وأم الولد إذا قتلت مولاها فإنها تعتق ولا شيء عليها إن كان القتل خطأ ؛ كذا في شرح الطحاوي. وذكر قاضيخان في كتاب الحجر أن المحجور عليه يصح تدبيره وبموته سفيهاً يعتق المدبر ويسعى في قيمته مدبراً، فإن كانت قيمته مدبراً عشرة يسعى في عشرة اهـ. مع أنه نقل قبله أن وصية المحجور عليه جائزة من ثلث ماله. وأطلق في الموت فشمل الحكمي بالردة بأن ارتد المولى عن الإسلام. والعياذ بالله تعالى ـ ولحق بدار الحرب لأنها مع اللحاق تجري مجرى الموت، وكذا المستأمن إذا اشترى عبداً في دار الإسلام فدبره ولحق بدار الحرب فاسترق الحربي عتق مدبره؛ كذا في البدائع. وأطلق في التدبير فشمل ما إذا كان في الصحة أو في المرض لأنه وصية في الحالين ويعتبر من ثلث المال يوم مات المولى كما في الوصايا وفي المحيط : إن المدبر يعتق في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياة المولى اهـ. وهو التحقيق وعليه يحمل كلامهم . والمؤنث كلفظ المملوك قوله : ( حتى لو قتله المدبر) كذا في النسخ وهو تحريف وصوابه حذف الضمير من «قتله» والمدبر اسم فاعل قوله : (مع أنه نقل قبله الخ قال في النهر : ولعل الفرق هو أن التدبير الآن بخلاف الوصية فإنها بعد الموت وله الرجوع قبله فلا إتلاف فيها .
His saying: (And with his death he is freed from his third) meaning upon the death of the master, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's wealth, because of what we have narrated from his statement (peace be upon him): 'He is free from the third,' and because tadbir is a will, since it is a donation attached to the time of death, and the ruling is not established in the present, so it is executed from the third. And because it is a will, so if the mudabbar kills him, he works to earn his entire value, because there is no will for the killer. And umm al-walad if she kills her master, she is freed and nothing is due from her if the killing was accidental; thus in Sharh al-Tahawi. Qadi Khan mentioned in Kitab al-Hajr that it is valid for an interdicted person to make tadbir, and upon his death (even if he was foolish), the mudabbar is freed and works to earn his value as a mudabbar. If his value as a mudabbar is ten, he works to earn ten. Although it was quoted before him that the will of an interdicted person is valid from one-third of his wealth. And (death) is general, including the legal death by apostasy: if the master apostatizes from Islam (may Allah protect us) and joins the abode of war, because joining is like death. Likewise, a musta'min who buys a slave in Dar al-Islam and makes tadbir for him, then joins Dar al-Harb, and the Harbi enslaves him, his mudabbar is freed; thus in al-Bada'i. And (tadbir) is general, including whether it was done in health or illness, because it is a will in both cases, and it is considered from one-third of the wealth on the day the master died, as in wills. And in al-Muhit: The mudabbar is freed in the last part of the master's life. That is the verified position, and their statements are interpreted accordingly. And the feminine is like the word 'mamluk'. His saying: (Even if the mudabbar kills him) – thus in copies, but it is a corruption; the correct is to drop the pronoun from 'yagtuluhu' and 'mudabbar' is an active participle. His saying: (Although it was quoted before him etc.) said in al-Nahr: Perhaps the difference is that tadbir is different from a will, because a will is after death and he can revoke it before, so there is no loss in it.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from hadith, establishing that the mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's estate upon death, because tadbir is considered a will (wasaya). The proof includes the hadith 'He is free from the third.' It also discusses special cases: if the mudabbar kills his master, he must work to earn his full value (since a killer cannot benefit from a will); the ruling for umm walad (if she kills accidentally, she becomes free without liability); tadbir of an interdicted person (mahjur) is valid, and the mudabbar works for his value; death includes legal death by apostasy (murtadd) and joining the dar al-harb; tadbir in health or illness is valid. The passage also clarifies that the mudabbar is freed at the final moment of the master's life. It ends with a textual correction: the phrase 'yagtuluhu al-mudabbar' should be read as 'yagtulu al-mudabbar' (active participle). The difference between tadbir and wasiyya is noted from al-Nahr.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A will; tadbir is considered a will because it is a donation conditioned on death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual proof for the Hanafi ruling that the mudabbar is freed from one-third?
A) Quran 4:11
B) Hadith 'He is free from the third'
C) Analogy to sale
D) Ijma of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Tadbir is a will, so the mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's estate, as proven by the hadith 'He is free from the third'.

Special Cases in Tadbir: Killing, Interdiction, Apostasy, and Timing
Expands the tadbir rule with special cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how special circumstances (killing, interdiction, apostasy, timing) modify the tadbir ruling and apply the correct sa'y compensation.

Core Idea
Tadbir's will-like nature means the killer cannot benefit, the mahjur's tadbir is valid with sa'y, and apostasy triggers immediate freedom from one-third.

The basic tadbir rule is tested by several edge cases: when the mudabbar kills his master, when the master was interdicted (mahjur), when the master apostatizes, and when the declaration was made in health or illness. Each case illustrates a consistent principle: tadbir is a will, so legal death and liability affect the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify each special scenario
List all the special cases mentioned: mudabbar kills master, umm walad kills master, mahjur makes tadbir, master apostatizes (murtadd) or joins dar al-harb, tadbir in health vs. illness, timing of freedom (last part of life).
2
State the ruling modification for each
For each scenario, state what happens to the mudabbar's freedom and any compensation (sa'y).
3
Explain the underlying legal principle
Analyze why the ruling changes: killer cannot inherit/have will; mahjur's tadbir is valid because it doesn't cause immediate loss; apostasy is legal death; health/illness does not affect the will nature.
4
Note the timing and corrections
The mudabbar is freed at the last moment of master's life. Also note the textual correction about the pronoun in 'yagtulu'.
5
Summarize the practical effect
For each case, summarize the final practical status of the mudabbar (freed completely, freed with sa'y, or not freed).

The Mudabbar's Legal Status During Sa'yah: An Intra-Hanafi Refinement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mudabbar's status during sa'yah, with critical refinement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the mudabbar's legal status during sa'yah, apply the refined view that he is a free debtor, and explain the practical consequences regarding testimony and tort liability.

Core Idea
The mudabbar is free upon the master's death; his sa'yah is for a debt, not freedom.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: what is the legal status of a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death) when he must work (sa'yah) to pay a value exceeding one-third of the estate? Imam Abu Hanifa likened him to a mukatib (a slave working for freedom), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) considered him a free debtor. The later scholar al-Shurunbulali refines the position, arguing that the mudabbar is already free by the master's death, so his status during sa'yah is that of a free debtor. Understanding this refinement clarifies rules of testimony, marriage, and tort liability for the mudabbar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The mudabbar must work (sa'yah) when the master is poor (only asset is the slave) or in debt (debt consumes the estate). In the first case, he works for two-thirds of his value; in the second, for the full value.
This is because the tadbir is a will, and debt takes precedence over the will.
2
State the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that during sa'yah, the mudabbar is like a mukatib (a slave contracted for freedom). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he is a free debtor.
3
Note the practical consequences
Under Imam's view: testimony is not accepted, he cannot marry without permission, and blood money for his tort is on the heir (the one he works for). Under Sahibayn's view: testimony is accepted, he can marry, and blood money is on his tribal group (aqila).
4
Understand al-Shurunbulali's critique
Al-Shurunbulali in his treatise 'Iqadh Dhuwi al-diraya' argues that the statements suggesting the mudabbar is like a mukatib contradict the clear text of Imam Abu Hanifa. The real dispute was about divisibility of emancipation (tajazzi al-itaq), not about the mudabbar. The mudabbar is completely freed by the master's death.
He cites al-Siraj: the mustas'i (one required to work) is of two types: those working to free their necks (like mukatib) and those working for a replacement value (like free debtor).
5
Apply the refined view
The later adopted position (mufta bihi) is that the mudabbar is a free debtor during sa'yah. Therefore, his testimony is accepted, he can marry, and blood money for his tort is on his aqila.
This is supported by the hadith that the mudabbar is free from one-third and by the definition of tadbir as immediate freedom upon death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويسعى في ثلثيه لو فقيراً أو كله لو مديوناً) أي يسعى المدبر للورثة في ثلثي قيمته لو كان المولى فقيراً ليس له مال إلا هو، وفي جميع قيمته لو كان المولى مديوناً ديناً يستغرق ماله لما ذكرنا أنه وصية ومحل نفاذها الثلث والدين مقدم عليها. اعلم أن المدبر في زمن سعايته كالمكاتب عند الإمام وعندهما حر مديون فتتفرع الأحكام فلا تقبل شهادته ولا يزوج نفسه عنده لما في المجمع من الجنايات ولو ترك مدبراً فقتل خطأ. وهو يسعى للوارث فعليه قيمته لوليه وقالا ديته على عاقلته ا هـ . وهكذا في الكافي وعلله بما ذكرناه. وكذا المنجز عتقه في مرض الموت إذا لم يخرج من الثلث فإنه في زمن سعايته كالمكاتب عنده فلا تقبل شهادته كما في شهادات ،البزازية وحكم جنايته كجناية المكاتب كما في شرح المجمع للمصنف. وقولهم هنا يعتق المدبر بموت المولى من ثلث المال يدل عليه فإن لم يخرج من الثلث لم يعتق حتى يسعى ويؤديها. قيدنا بكون الدين مستغرقاً لأن الدين لو كان أقل من
قوله : (اعلم أن المدبر في زمن سعايته الخ) قال العلامة الشرنبلالي في رسالته «إيقاظ ذوي الدراية لوصف من كلف السعاية بعد نقله لكلام المؤلف هنا أقول : قد صدرت تلك العبارات وهي مخالفة لنص الإمام وإن رد مثلها مسنداً للإمام فاختلف النقل عنه ولم تحرره الأعلام. والمقرر أن الخلاف بين الإمام وصاحبيه في تجزي الإعتاق وحصول العتق وعدمه فيمن أعتق بعضه لا فيمن أعتق كله منجزاً أو معلقاً على شرط فوجد في مرض أو صحته وسعايته بعده سعاية حر مديون كالمدبر إذا لم يخرج من الثلث . قال في السراج المستسعي عند أبي حنيفة على ضربين : كل من يسعى في تخليص رقبته فهو كالمكاتب، وكل من يسعى في بدل رقبته الذي لزم بالعتق أو في قيمة رقبته لأجل بدل شرط عليه أو لدين ثبت في رقبته فهو كالحر ا هـ. ولا شك أن المدبر قد عتق كله بموت المولى فهو وإن سعى يسعى وهو حر فلم يكن كالمكاتب وما في المجمع قد يقال إنه مفرع على ما قيل إن المستسعي كالمكاتب وليس على عمومه لما علمت فموجب جنايته على عاقلة مولاه للنص على حريته بمجرد موت سيده وما عزى إلى البزازية لم أره فيها وعبارتها لا تقبل شهادة المدبر انتهت . ووصفة بالمدبر حقيقة إنما هو في حياة سيده أما بعدها فهو حر مقبول الشهادة. نعم قال في فصول العمادي وتهذيب الخاصي : المريض إذا أعتق عبداً في مرض موته ولا مال له سواه فعتقه موقوف عند أبي حنيفة حتى إذا شهد لا تقبل لأنه من التصرفات التي لا تحتمل الفسخ بعد النفاذ فتوقف ا هـ. أيضاً مأخوذ من التشبيه ويعارضه ما مر عن الإمام من تقسيم المستسعي إلى قسمين، ولئن صح نقله عن الإمام فالوجه النقل الموافق لنص الشارع ولتعريف التدبير قال ابن الهمام: التدبير شرعاً العتق الموقع بعد الموت في المملوك معلقاً بالموت مطلقاً لفظاً أو معنى ا هـ. والمعلق ينزل بوجود شرطه كملاً. وروى ابن عمر النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم قال إن المدبر لا يباع ولا يوهب ولا يورث وهو حر من الثلث. وقال الزيلعي : المدبر تعلق عتقه بنفس الموت أي موت سيده فلا يشترط فيه إعتاق أحد ثم قال : وبموت المولى يعتق من ثلث ماله وإنما يسعى إذا لم يكن له مال
His statement: (And he works to pay two-thirds if he is poor, or all of it if he is in debt) meaning: the mudabbar works for the heirs in two-thirds of his value if the master was poor having no property except him, and in all of his value if the master was in debt with a debt that consumes his property, because, as we mentioned, it is a will and its place of enforcement is one-third, and debt takes precedence over it. Know that the mudabbar during the period of his working is like a mukatib according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he is a free debtor. Thus legal rulings branch out: his testimony is not accepted, and he does not marry himself off according to him, as in al-Majma' regarding injuries. If a mudabbar kills by mistake while he is working for the heir, then according to him his blood money is on his heir, but they said his blood money is on his tribal group. Likewise, one who is emancipated in terminal illness if it does not come out of one-third, then during his working period he is like a mukatib according to him, so his testimony is not accepted as in the Shahadat of al-Bazzaziyya, and the ruling on his injury is like that of a mukatib as in Sharh al-Majma' by the author. Their statement here that the mudabbar is freed by the master's death from one-third of the property indicates that, if it does not come out of one-third, he is not freed until he works and pays it. We restricted it to the debt being consuming because if the debt were less than... His statement: (Know that the mudabbar during his working period etc.) al-Allama al-Shurunbulali said in his treatise 'Iqadh Dhuwi al-diraya li-wasf man kullifa al-sa'yah after quoting the author's words here: I say: those statements have appeared, and they contradict the text of Imam Abu Hanifa, and if the like of them is attributed to the Imam, the transmission differed about him and the learned scholars did not refine it. The established view is that the disagreement between the Imam and his two companions is concerning the divisibility of emancipation and the occurrence or non-occurrence of freedom for one who emancipates part of his slave, not for one who emancipates all of him immediately or conditionally in health or illness, and his working thereafter is the working of a free debtor, like the mudabbar if he does not come out of one-third. He said in al-Siraj: The one who is required to work (mustas'i) according to Abu Hanifa is of two types: everyone who works to free his neck (i.e., to earn his freedom) is like a mukatib, and everyone who works for the replacement of his neck that was necessitated by emancipation, or for the value of his neck due to a condition placed on him, or for a debt that is fixed on his neck, is like a free person. End. There is no doubt that the mudabbar has been completely freed by the master's death, so even if he works, he works while free, so he is not like a mukatib. What is in al-Majma' may be said to be branched on the view that the mustas'i is like a mukatib, and it is not general as you have learned. Thus the obligation of his injury is on the tribal group of his master due to the text on his freedom by the mere death of his master. What is attributed to al-Bazzaziyya, I did not see it in it, and its wording is: the testimony of the mudabbar is not accepted, end. The description 'mudabbar' in reality is during the life of his master; after that he is free and his testimony is accepted. Yes, he said in Fusul al-Imadi and Tahdhib al-Khasi: the sick person if he emancipates a slave in his terminal illness and he has no property other than him, then his emancipation is suspended according to Abu Hanifa, so if he testifies, it is not accepted because it is among actions that cannot be rescinded after execution, so it is suspended. End. Also it is taken from analogy, and it is contradicted by what was reported from the Imam about dividing the mustas'i into two categories. And if his transmission from the Imam is authentic, then the preferred view is to follow what conforms to the text of the Lawgiver and to the definition of tadbir. Ibn al-Humam said: Tadbir according to law is the emancipation that is effected after death in the owned slave, suspended on death unconditionally in wording or meaning. End. What is suspended occurs upon the existence of its condition completely. And Ibn Umar narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: The mudabbar is not sold, not given as a gift, not inherited, and he is free from one-third. Al-Zayla'i said: The mudabbar's emancipation is attached to death itself, i.e., the death of his master, so the emancipation of anyone is not a condition. Then he said: By the master's death he is freed from one-third of his property, and he only works if he has no property.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the legal status of the mudabbar during the period of sa'yah (working to pay the value that exceeds one-third). The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins by explaining the basic ruling: if the master is poor (no other property) and has only this slave, the mudabbar works for the heirs to pay two-thirds of his value (since one-third is the will that is executed). If the master is in debt that consumes his entire estate, the mudabbar works to pay the full value because debt takes precedence over the will. The commentary then raises the issue of the mudabbar's legal capacity during sa'yah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the mudabbar is like a mukatib (a slave contracted for freedom) during this period — his testimony is not accepted, and he cannot marry without permission, and if he commits a homicide the blood money is on his heir (the one for whom he works). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), he is a free debtor — his testimony is accepted, he can marry, and his blood money is on his tribal group (aqila). The author notes that the same applies to a sick person who emancipates a slave in terminal illness if the slave's value exceeds one-third. Al-Shurunbulali then enters with a critical refinement in his treatise. He argues that the statements suggesting the mudabbar is like a mukatib during sa'yah contradict the clear text of Imam Abu Hanifa. The real disagreement between Imam and Sahibayn is about the divisibility of emancipation (tajazzi al-itaq) — i.e., when someone emancipates part of a slave. But the mudabbar is completely freed by the master's death; his sa'yah is not to earn freedom but to pay what is due to the heirs. Thus, he is free during sa'yah, not like a mukatib. Shurunbulali cites al-Siraj which divides the mustas'i into two: those working to free their necks (like mukatib) and those working for a replacement value (like free debtor). The mudabbar falls into the second category. He supports this with the hadith that the mudabbar is free from one-third, and with definitions from Ibn al-Humam and al-Zayla'i. The passage concludes that once the master dies, the mudabbar is free; his testimony is accepted, and his blood money is on the aqila. The reliance upon the refinement is that the mudabbar's legal status is that of a freeman, not a mukatib.

Key Terms
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon his master's death (tadbir). He becomes free upon the master's death if the master's estate can bear his value from one-third.
السعاية (al-sa'yah): The mudabbar's working to earn money to pay the value that exceeds one-third of the estate, to the heirs.
المكاتب (al-mukatib): A slave who has contracted with his master to work and pay a specified sum to earn his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the refined position (mufta bihi) in this passage, what is the status of the mudabbar during sa'yah?
A) He is like a mukatib, his testimony is not accepted.
B) He is a free debtor, his testimony is accepted.
C) He remains a slave until he pays the full value.
D) He is a free person but cannot marry.

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar during sa'yah is a free debtor, not a slave, because he is already free by the master's death.

Conditional Tadbir and Its Rulings
Explaining the ruling on conditional tadbir and the value of mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on conditional tadbir, calculate the mudabbar's value according to the mufta bihi, and explain the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tadbir followed by kitaba.

Core Idea
A conditional tadbir is valid; the mudabbar's value is two-thirds of his slave value.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings of conditional tadbir (muqayyad). It explains that a tadbir conditioned on a specific event—like death in travel or after a period—is valid by istihsan, and the slave becomes free from one-third upon the condition's fulfillment. It also addresses the valuation of a mudabbar and the intra-Hanafi differences when tadbir is combined with a kitaba contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition in tadbir
Look for phrases like 'if I die from this travel' or 'after ten years'. These make the tadbir muqayyad (conditional).
The condition must be a future event tied to the master's death.
2
Validate the tadbir by istihsan
Understand that conditional tadbir is valid by istihsan despite the condition's uncertainty, because the intent of emancipation upon death is clear and the condition is attached to death.
The qiyas is with absolute tadbir; the illa is the intention of freedom upon death.
3
Determine the mudabbar's value
Apply the mufta bihi that the value of a mudabbar is two-thirds of his value as an ordinary slave (qinn). Note the alternative of half chosen by al-Sadr al-Shahid.
This affects the one-third bequest limit: the slave's freedom consumes one-third of the estate based on his reduced value.
4
Resolve tadbir+kitaba conflict
In the scenario where a mudabbar is also given a kitaba, the Hanafi imams differ: Imam Abu Hanifa gives the slave a choice; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad assign the lesser obligation.
This ikhtilaf affects how much the slave must work to earn his freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويباع لو قال إن مت من سفري أو من مرضي أو إلى عشر سنين أو عشرين سنة أو أنت حر بعد موت فلان ويعتق إن وجد الشرط) بيان للمدبر المقيد وأحكامه. وحاصله أن يعلق عتقه بموته على صفة لا بمطلقه كتقييده بموته في سفر أو مرض مخصوص أو بمدة معينة يعيشان إلى مثلها أو بزيادة شيء بعد موت المولى كقوله إذا مت وغسلت أو كفنت ودفنت فأنت فيعتق إذا مات استحساناً حر من الثلث لأنه يغسل ويكفن ويدفن عقيب الموت. وقدمنا أن المفتى به أن قيمة المدبر ثلثا قيمته قناً، واختار الصدر الشهيد أنها النصف، وفي الولوالجية وهو المختار لأن الانتفاع بالمملوك نوعان : انتفاع بعينه وانتفاع ببدله وهو الثمن والانتفاع بالعين قائم وبالبدل فائت ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير : إذا دبره ثم كاتبه ثم مات المولى وهو يخرج من ثلثه عتق بالتدبير وسقطت عنه الكتابة فإن لم يكن له مال غيره فإنه يخير إن شاء سعى في جميع بدل الكتابة بجهة عقد الكتابة وإن شاء سعى في ثلثي قيمته بالتدبير. وهذا عند الإمام لأن العتق يتجزئ عنده وقد تلقاه جهتا حرية فيتخير أيهما شاء، وعند أبي يوسف يسعى في الأقل منهما بغير خيار، وعند محمد يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي قيمته ومن ثلثي بدل الكتابة ولو كاتبه ثم دبره فعند أبي حنيفة يتخير بين أن يسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي بدل الكتابة وعندهما يسعى في أقلهما عينا وتمامه فيه. وذكر في الحاوي القدسي : لو قال لعبده أنت . أمر بالبيان فإن مات أو مدبر حر على ما كان فإن كان القول منه في الصحة عتق نصفه من جميع المال ونصفه من الثلث اهـ .
His statement: (And he is sold if he said: If I die from my travel, or from my illness, or until ten years or twenty years, or you are free after the death of so-and-so, and he becomes free if the condition is found) Explanation of the conditional tadbir and its rulings. Its summary: that he suspends his freedom upon his death with a description, not on an absolute basis, like restricting it to his death in travel or a specific illness, or to a specific period as long as they both live to its like, or to an addition of something after the master's death, like his saying: When I die and I am washed, shrouded, and buried, then you are free. So he becomes free when he dies by istihsan, free from one-third, because he is washed, shrouded, and buried immediately after death. And we have previously mentioned that the mufta bihi is that the value of a mudabbar is two-thirds of his value as a slave (qinn). Al-Sadr al-Shahid chose that it is half, and in al-Walwaljjya it is the chosen view, because the benefit from a owned slave is of two types: benefit by his 'ayn (person) and benefit by his badal (substitute) which is the price. The benefit by the 'ayn is existent, and by the badal is lost. End. And in Fath al-Qadir: If he made him a mudabbar, then made a kitaba contract with him, then the master died while he (the slave) comes out of one-third, he is freed by the tadbir and the kitaba falls. If he has no property other than him, then he is given a choice: if he wishes, he works for all of the kitaba price according to the kitaba contract, and if he wishes, he works for two-thirds of his value by tadbir. This is according to Imam because emancipation is divisible according to him, and he has come across two sources of freedom, so he chooses whichever he wishes. According to Abu Yusuf, he works for the lesser of the two without choice. According to Muhammad, he works for the lesser of two-thirds of his value and two-thirds of the kitaba price. And if he made kitaba and then tadbir, then according to Abu Hanifa he has the choice between working for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitaba price, while according to them (the two) he works for the lesser of the two specifically. And its completion is in it. And it is mentioned in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: If he said to his slave: 'You are...' clarification, then if he dies or is a mudabbar, free as he was, then if the statement was in health, he is freed half from all property and half from one-third. End.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings on conditional tadbir (muqayyad). The matn states that if the master says something like 'You are free if I die from this travel,' or 'if I die from this illness,' or 'after ten years,' or 'you are free after the death of so-and-so,' then the slave becomes free upon the occurrence of the condition, but the tadbir is still treated as a will from one-third. The author explains that such conditional statements are valid and the slave becomes free by istihsan (juristic preference) because the described events are immediate upon death (like washing, shrouding, burial) or are future events. The discussion then shifts to the value of the mudabbar for calculation. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that the value of a mudabbar is two-thirds of his value as an ordinary slave (qinn), because his benefit is diminished due to the pending freedom; neither the owner nor the slave can be fully used. Al-Sadr al-Shahid preferred half. Al-Walwaliji chooses two-thirds on the basis that the owner suffers loss of both the person and the price. The passage then discusses the case of tadbir followed by kitaba (contract for freedom). If the master dies while the slave has both a tadbir and a kitaba, and the slave's value is within one-third of the estate, he is freed by tadbir and the kitaba falls. If there is no other property, the slave has a choice between working according to the kitaba or working for two-thirds of his value by tadbir, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because emancipation is divisible. According to Abu Yusuf, he works for the lesser of the two amounts. According to Muhammad, he works for the lesser of two-thirds of his value and two-thirds of the kitaba price. Similarly, if kitaba came first, then tadbir, the same ikhtilaf applies. Finally, a quote from al-Hawi al-Qudsi about a slave who is declared mudabbar in health but without specification; it says he becomes free half from all property and half from one-third, which appears to be a separate ruling.

Key Terms
المدبر المقيد (al-mudabbar al-muqayyad): A tadbir that is conditioned upon a specific circumstance (e.g., 'if I die from this travel').
قيمته مدبراً (qimtihi mudabbaran): The value of the slave as a mudabbar, which is less than his value as an ordinary slave due to the pending freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Full value as a slave
B) Half value as a slave
C) Two-thirds of his value as a slave
D) One-third of his value as a slave

Key Takeaway
Conditional tadbir is valid, and the value of a mudabbar is two-thirds of his slave value according to the mufta bihi.

Valuation of a Mudabbar for Sa'y: The Two-Thirds Rule
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mudabbar valuation for sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi value of a mudabbar and explain the Hanafi rationale for the two-thirds rule.

Core Idea
A mudabbar's value for debt payment is two-thirds of his qinn value, preserving the master's benefit from the slave's person.

When a mudabbar's master dies with debts, the mudabbar must work (sa'y) to pay those debts. But what value should be used to determine how much he must earn? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: should the mudabbar be valued as an ordinary slave (qinn) or at a reduced price due to his impending freedom? We explore the reasoning that led the later Hanafi school to adopt the two-thirds rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The mudabbar is a slave promised freedom upon the master's death. When the master dies with debts, the mudabbar must work to pay them. The key question is: what is his value for this calculation?
The value determines how much he must earn and how much is a bequest.
2
Recognize the dispute
Al-Quduri summarized the value without specifying whether it is as a qinn or mudabbar. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (in Kitab al-Hajr) explicitly states the mudabbar works for his value as a mudabbar. Later scholars disagreed: al-Sadr al-Shahid chose half the qinn value, while the mufta bihi is two-thirds.
The dispute is not about the obligation of sa'y, but about the valuation base.
3
Understand the positions
List the three views: (1) Muhammad: value as mudabbar (no numeric fraction given but implies reduced). (2) al-Sadr al-Shahid: half of qinn value. (3) mufta bihi: two-thirds of qinn value.
The mufta bihi is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
4
Grasp the rationale
The rationale from al-Walwalijiyyah: a master's benefit from a slave is twofold—benefit from the slave's person (work, services) and benefit from his sale price. Tadbir cancels the sale price (because the slave will be freed), but the personal benefit remains. Since one of two benefits is lost, two-thirds of the qinn value is considered lost. This is why the mudabbar's value is two-thirds.
This reasoning is specific to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السفيه ومات قيمته فإنه يسعى في قدر الدين والزيادة على الدين ثلثها وصية ويسعى في ثلثي الزيادة؛ كذا في شرح الطحاوي وذكر في المجتبى أن القدوري اجمل القيمة ولم يبين أنه يسعى في قيمته قناً أو مدبراً وذكر في بط أنه يسعى في قيمته مدبراً. وذكر محمد في كتاب الحجر إذا دبر ثم مات يسعى الغلام في قيمته مدبراً وليس عليه نقصان التدبير كالصالح إذا دبر وعليه ديون ا هـ . وقدمنا أن المفتى به أن قيمة المدبر ثلثا قيمته قناً، واختار الصدر الشهيد أنها النصف، وفي الولوالجية وهو المختار لأن الانتفاع بالمملوك نوعان : انتفاع بعينه وانتفاع ببدله وهو الثمن والانتفاع بالعين قائم وبالبدل فائت ا هـ .
Al-Sufayh [who] died; his value: he (the mudabbar) works to pay the amount of the debt, and the increase over the debt: one third of it is a bequest, and he works for two-thirds of the increase. Thus in Sharh al-Tahawi. And it is mentioned in al-Mujtaba that al-Quduri summarized the value and did not clarify whether he works for his value as a qinn (ordinary slave) or as a mudabbar. And it is mentioned in [؟] that he works for his value as a mudabbar. And Muhammad mentioned in Kitab al-Hajr: If he (the master) gives tadbir then dies, the boy works for his value as a mudabbar, and the decrease due to tadbir is not upon him, just as al-Salih if he gives tadbir and he has debts, end quote. And we have stated before that the mufta bihi is that the value of a mudabbar is two-thirds of his value as a qinn. And al-Sadr al-Shahid chose that it is half, and in al-Walwalijiyyah it is the preferred opinion because benefit from a owned person is of two kinds: benefit from his person and benefit from his substitute which is the price; benefit from the person is present while benefit from the substitute is absent. End quote.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage discusses the valuation of a mudabbar (a slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death) when the master dies with debts. The mudabbar must work (sa'y) to pay off the master's debts, but there is a dispute as to whether his value is assessed as an ordinary slave (qinn) or as a mudabbar (which has reduced value due to the anticipation of freedom). The text notes that al-Quduri did not specify, but Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, in Kitab al-Hajr, states that the mudabbar works for his value as a mudabbar, and the decrease from tadbir is not attributed to him. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a mudabbar's value is two-thirds of his value as a qinn, based on the reasoning that the master's benefit from a slave is twofold: benefit from the slave's person (which remains) and benefit from the slave's sale price (which is lost due to tadbir). Since the benefit from the person remains, only two-thirds of the value is considered lost. This is a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute where later scholars like al-Sadr al-Shahid preferred half, but the dominant view is two-thirds.

Key Terms
قيمة المدبر (qīmat al-mudabbar): The monetary value of a mudabbar slave, which is less than that of an ordinary slave due to the imminent freedom.
سعى (sa'ā): The mudabbar works to earn money to pay off the master's debts or to compensate heirs.
قناً (qinnan): An ordinary slave with full market value, not subject to tadbir.
تدبير (tadbir): The master's declaration that the slave will be free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, what is the value of a mudabbar relative to his qinn value?
A) Full value
B) Half
C) Two-thirds
D) One-third

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi value of a mudabbar for sa'y is two-thirds of his qinn value, based on the principle that the master's benefit from the slave's person remains while the benefit from the sale price is lost.

Conditional Tadbir and Its Rulings
Definition and ruling of conditional tadbir with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and ruling of conditional tadbir in Hanafi fiqh, and apply the istihsan reasoning to determine the slave's status.

Core Idea
A conditional tadbir is valid: the slave is freed from one-third upon the master's death if the condition is met.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the concept of conditional tadbir (al-mudabbar al-muqayyad)—where the master suspends the slave's freedom on his death but with a specific condition, such as dying in a particular journey or after being washed and buried. The ruling is that the slave becomes free if the condition occurs, but only from one-third of the estate, analogized to a bequest. The justification (istihsan) is that such conditions are automatically fulfilled after death. We will examine the types of conditions, the legal reasoning, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is a conditional tadbir (tadbir muqayyad) – the master declares that upon his death, the slave is free if a certain condition is met. This is a subset of tadbir (declaration of freedom after death).
Contrast with absolute tadbir (mudabbar mutlaq) where no condition is attached.
2
List the types of conditions mentioned
The passage lists several conditions: death from a specific travel or illness, death within a fixed period (e.g., ten years), or freedom after some event after the master's death (e.g., after washing and burial).
These conditions are attached to the master's death, not to the slave's action.
3
Determine the ruling and its basis
The ruling is that the slave becomes free upon the master's death if the condition is met, but the freedom is effective from one-third of the estate (like a bequest). The basis is istihsan: the condition (e.g., being washed) is inevitably fulfilled immediately after death, so it is treated as if it were absolute.
Qiyas would reject such conditional tadbir because the condition is not under the slave's control, but istihsan allows it due to common practice and benefit.
4
Note the practical consequence (one-third limit)
The slave's freedom is treated as a bequest (wasiyya), which cannot exceed one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. Thus, if the slave's value exceeds one-third, only one-third is freed, and the remaining is subject to the heirs' permission.
This is analogous to the rule for absolute tadbir as well.
5
Recognize the proof structure
The ruling is supported by istihsan (juristic preference), which overrides qiyas. The author uses the example of washing, shrouding, and burial – actions that necessarily occur after death – to show the condition is always met.
This is a case of expansion (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the types and ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويباع لو قال إن مت من سفري أو من مرضي أو إلى عشر سنين أو عشرين سنة أو أنت حر بعد موت فلان ويعتق إن وجد الشرط) بيان للمدبر المقيد وأحكامه. وحاصله أن يعلق عتقه بموته على صفة لا بمطلقه كتقييده بموته في سفر أو مرض مخصوص أو بمدة معينة يعيشان إلى مثلها أو بزيادة شيء بعد موت المولى كقوله إذا مت وغسلت وكفنت ودفنت فأنت فيعتق إذا مات استحساناً حر من الثلث لأنه يغسل ويكفن ويدفن عقيب الموت.
He is sold. If he (the master) says: 'If I die from my travel, or from my illness, or within ten years, or twenty years, or you are free after the death of so-and-so,' and he becomes free if the condition is found. This is an explanation of the conditional mudabbar and its rulings. In summary, he (the master) suspends his freedom upon his death with a description, not absolutely, such as restricting it to death in a specific travel or illness, or to a specific period within which they both might live, or to something additional after the master's death, like his saying: 'When I die, and I am washed, shrouded, and buried, then you are free.' So he becomes free upon death by istihsan, free from one-third, because he is washed, shrouded, and buried immediately after death.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage defines conditional tadbir (al-mudabbar al-muqayyad) and its rulings. The master suspends the slave's freedom upon his own death with a specific condition, such as death during a journey, from a particular illness, within a set number of years, or after some event after death (like washing and burial). The ruling is that the slave becomes free upon the master's death if the condition is met, but the freedom is limited to one-third of the estate (since it is a bequest). The reasoning (istihsan) is that these actions (washing, shrouding, burial) occur immediately after death, so the condition is virtually always fulfilled. This is a ruling with proof from istihsan, and it is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Key Terms
تذبير (tadbir): The master's declaration that a slave will be free after his (the master's) death.
مدبر مقيد (mudabbar muqayyad): A tadbir that is conditional on a specific event related to the master's death.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows a ruling that deviates from qiyas in favor of convenience or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In conditional tadbir, from which portion of the estate does the slave become free?
A) Full estate
B) Half
C) One-third
D) Whatever the master specifies

Key Takeaway
Conditional tadbir is valid in Hanafi law; the slave is freed from one-third upon the master's death if the condition is met, supported by istihsan.

The Phrase 'If I Die or Am Killed' in Tadbir
Resolving whether 'if I die or am killed' creates absolute or conditional tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the tadbir phrase 'if I die or am killed' and identify which view is preferred and why.

Core Idea
Suspending tadbir on 'die or be killed' creates absolute tadbir in meaning, not conditional.

When a master says 'if I die or am killed, you are free,' does this create a valid tadbir? Abu Hanifa held that the oscillation between two possibilities prevents tadbir, but later Hanafi masters preferred Zufar's view that it is absolute. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the exact wording: 'if I die or am killed.' Determine whether this creates a tadbir (freedom upon death) and if so, whether it is absolute or conditional.
The issue hinges on the disjunction 'or' (أو).
2
Identify the Three Hanafi Positions
List Abu Hanifa's view (no tadbir), Abu Yusuf's view (absolute tadbir), and Zufar's view (absolute tadbir, later preferred).
Abu Yusuf and Zufar agree on absolute tadbir but differ slightly in reasoning.
3
Analyze the Reasoning
Examine why Abu Hanifa sees uncertainty (taraddud) and why Zufar sees absolute death in meaning (fi al-ma'na mawt mutlaq).
Zufar argues that death will occur in one of the two ways, so the intended meaning is freedom upon any death.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Recognize that Fath al-Qadir prefers Zufar's view, making it the operative ruling for fatwa.
Tarjih is based on the stronger analogy to absolute death.
5
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Understand the practical effect: if absolute tadbir, the slave is freed from one-third and cannot be sold; if not tadbir, the slave remains a normal asset.
The difference affects the slave's status and the heir's rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال قبل أن يتقرر ملك الوارث أو بترداده بين الموت والقتل كقوله إذا مت أو قتلت فليس بمدبر مدبراً ويجوز بيعه. وقال مطلق عند أبي يوسف لأنه علقه بأحد الشيئين والقتل وإن كان موتاً فالموت ليس بقتل، وتعليقه بأحد الأمرين يمنع كونه عزيمة في أحدهما خاصة فلا يصير زفر: هو مدبر مطلق. ورجحه في فتح القدير بأنه أحسن لأن التعليق في المعنى بمطلق موته لأنه لا تردد في كون الكائن أحد الأمرين من الموت قتلاً أو غير قتل، فهو في المعنى مطلق الموت كيفما كان.
And he (Abu Hanifa) said: Before the heir's ownership is established, or due to its (the condition's) oscillation between death and killing, like his saying: 'If I die or am killed,' he (the slave) is not a mudabbar; he is sold. And Abu Yusuf said: It is absolute tadbir, because he (the master) suspended it upon one of two things, and killing, even if it is death, death is not killing; and suspending upon one of two things prevents it from being a determination in one of them specifically, so it does not become [conditional]. Zufar said: It is absolute tadbir. And it (Zufar's view) was preferred in Fath al-Qadir because it is better, for the suspension in meaning is upon his absolute death, since there is no hesitation that what occurs is one of the two: death by killing or otherwise, so in meaning it is absolute death however it occurs.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage discusses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the phrase 'if I die or am killed.' Abu Hanifa held that this is not tadbir at all, because the condition is uncertain (oscillating between two possibilities), so the slave can be sold. Abu Yusuf considered it absolute tadbir (mutlaq) because the master did not specify which death; the condition is on one of two, so it is not specific enough to be conditional. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) also considered it absolute tadbir, and this view was preferred in Fath al-Qadir because the essential meaning is freedom upon any death, regardless of manner. The passage then critiques the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq for inconsistency with his ruling in nikah (temporary marriage) where he considered such phrasing as temporal. The commentary defends that in nikah the temporal aspect is considered for prohibition, while here the intended meaning of death is considered absolute. This is a critical refinement (hasiyah) as it reconciles apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A contract by which a master declares that his slave will be free upon the master's death.
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute; here meaning the tadbir applies to any death, not conditional on a specific manner.
تردد (taraddud): Oscillation or hesitation; here refers to the wording's doubt between two possibilities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in Fath al-Qadir, the phrase 'if I die or am killed' creates:
A) No tadbir
B) Conditional tadbir
C) Absolute tadbir
D) A bequest

Key Takeaway
The disjunction 'or' in a tadbir phrase does not prevent the tadbir; the intended meaning is absolute death, so the slave becomes mudabbar absolutely.

Conditional and Time-Limited Tadbir: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional and time-limited tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a mudabbar muqayyad and mutlaq, and state the Hanafi positions on conditional tadbir.

Core Idea
A tadbir conditional on 'die or killed' does not create a mudabbar; but a time limit that is unrealistic makes it absolute.

Tadbir is a contract that grants a slave freedom upon the master's death. But what if the master says 'if I die or am killed'? Or 'if I die within ten years'? The Hanafi school has internal disagreements on whether such conditions produce a mudabbar (who cannot be sold) or leave the slave ordinary property. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, Zufar, and later preferred views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage tackles two distinct scenarios: (1) tadbir conditioned on 'die or killed', and (2) tadbir with a time limit (e.g., within 10, 20, or 100 years). Recognize that each has its own ruling and ikhtilaf.
The primary dispute is over whether freedom is attached to death alone or to two alternatives.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position on conditional tadbir
According to Abu Hanifa (supported by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), saying 'if I die or am killed, you are free' does NOT make the slave a mudabbar. The attachment is to two alternatives, not death alone, so the tadbir does not take effect. The slave can be sold.
The passage quotes Abu Hanifa's reasoning via Abu Yusuf.
3
State Zufar's counter and the tarjih
Zufar argues that both alternatives (death by killing or natural death) result in death, so in meaning it is absolute death; hence the tadbir is absolute. The author of Fath al-Qadir prefers Zufar's view, but later fatwa sides with Abu Hanifa.
Know that Zufar's view is considered stronger by some but not the mufta bihi.
4
Apply the ruling to time-limited tadbir
If the master says 'you are free if I die within ten/twenty years', it is a restricted tadbir (muqayyad) — the slave can be sold. But if the time is unrealistic (e.g., 100 years, which the master will not likely outlive), it becomes absolute tadbir (mutlaq) according to a riwaya from Hasan ibn Ziyad. The later chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that even realistic time limits create absolute tadbir, but al-Walwaliji rejects this.
The commentator defends Kanz's consistency: timing in marriage invalidates but timing in tadbir does not, because the meaning (death) is perpetual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتق باب التدبير
مت أو قتلت فليس بمدبر مدبراً ويجوز بيعه . وقال قبل أن يتقرر ملك الوارث أو بترداده بين الموت والقتل كقوله إذا مطلق عند أبي يوسف لأنه علقه بأحد الشيئين والقتل وإن كان موتاً فالموت ليس بقتل، وتعليقه بأحد الأمرين يمنع كونه عزيمة في أحدهما خاصة فلا يصير زفر: هو مدبر مطلق. ورجحه في فتح القدير بأنه أحسن لأن التعليق في المعنى بمطلق موته لأنه لا تردد في كون الكائن أحد الأمرين من الموت قتلاً أو غير قتل، فهو في المعنى مطلق الموت كيفما كان وقيد بقوله إلى عشر سنين أو عشرين سنة لأنه لو قال إلى مائة سنة ومثله لا يعيش إليها في الغالب فهو مدبر مطلق لأنه كالكائن لا محالة وهذا رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة. وفي التبيين أنه المختار لكن ذكر قاضيخان أن على قول أصحابنا هو مدبر مقيد وهكذا ذكره في الينابيع وجوامع الفقه وفي فتح القدير: إن المصنف كالمناقض فإنه في النكاح اعتبره توقيتاً وأبطل به النكاح وهنا جعله تأبيداً موجباً للتدبير ا.هـ. وقد يجاب عنه بأنه في باب النكاح اعتبره توقيتاً للنهي عن النكاح الموقت، ولا شك أنه موقت صورة فالاحتياط في منعه تقديماً للمحرم على المبيح لأن النظر إلى الصورة يحرمه وإلى المعنى يبيحه، وأما هنا فنظر إلى التأبيد المعنوي ولا مانع منه فإن الأصل اعتبار المعنى ما لم يمنع مانع فلا تناقض ولذا كان هو المختار وإن كان الولوالجي جزم بأنه ليس بمدبر مطلق تسوية بينه وبين النكاح.
Chapter of Manumission, Section of Tadbir: If [the master says] 'If I die or am killed, then you are not a mudabbar' — it is permissible to sell him. He (Abu Hanifa) said before the heir's right is established, or due to hesitation between death and killing, like saying 'you are free unconditionally' according to Abu Yusuf, because he attached it to one of two things; killing, although it is death, death is not killing, and attaching to one of two prevents it being a resolve for one specifically, so it does not become [tadbir]. Zufar: he is an absolute mudabbar. It is preferred in Fath al-Qadir that this is better, because the attachment is in meaning to his absolute death, since there is no hesitation regarding the occurrence of one of the two — death by killing or not — so in meaning it is absolute death, however it occurs. And he restricted it by saying 'up to ten years' or 'twenty years' because if he said 'up to one hundred years' and someone like him generally does not live to that, then he is an absolute mudabbar, because it is inevitably occurring. This is a riwaya of Hasan from Abu Hanifa. In al-Tabyin it is the chosen view, but Qadikhan mentioned that according to our associates he is a restricted mudabbar, and similarly stated in al-Yanabi' and Jami' al-Fiqh. In Fath al-Qadir: that the author [of Kanz] appears contradictory, for in marriage he considered timing and invalidated marriage by it, while here he made it perpetual leading to tadbir. End. And it may be answered that in the chapter of marriage he considered timing because of the prohibition of temporary marriage, and it is undoubtedly timed in form, so caution is in its prohibition, giving precedence to the prohibited over the permissible, because looking at form forbids it and at meaning permits it. But here he looked at the perpetual meaning, and there is no preventing factor, for the principle is to consider meaning as long as no preventer prevents, so no contradiction. Hence it is the chosen view, even though al-Walwaliji definitively stated that it is not an absolute mudabbar, equating between it and marriage.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage discusses a key dispute on conditional tadbir. The matn states that a slave is not a mudabbar if the master says 'if I die or am killed, you are free' — rather the slave remains ordinary property and can be sold. Abu Hanifa's position (attributed to him by Abu Yusuf) is that such a conditional statement does not constitute tadbir because it attaches freedom to one of two alternatives, and the occurrence of one alternative (death by killing) is not certain; thus the tadbir does not take effect. Zufar counters that in reality, whichever occurs is death, so it is effectively absolute death and thus absolute tadbir. The author of Fath al-Qadir prefers Zufar's view. Then the text addresses tadbir with a time limit: if the master says 'you are free if I die within ten/twenty years', it is a restricted tadbir; but if the time is unrealistically long (100 years), it is absolute tadbir based on a riwaya from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa. A later discussion arises: the author of Kanz al-Daqaiq is accused of contradiction because he treats a time-limited marriage as invalid (mut'ah) but here treats a time-limited tadbir as absolute. The commentator defends the author, explaining that in marriage, the form is temporary, so prohibition prevails, but in tadbir, the meaning (death) is perpetual, so no contradiction. The chosen view is that time-limited tadbir is absolute, per al-Tabyin, though al-Walwaliji rejects this.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death, effective from the master's death.
مدبر مقيد (mudabbar muqayyad): A mudabbar whose freedom is tied to a specific condition, e.g., 'if I die in this journey' or 'within ten years'.
مدبر مطلق (mudabbar mutlaq): A mudabbar whose freedom is tied to the master's death without any restriction, making the slave unsellable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (al-mukhtar) in this passage, what is the ruling on a tadbir where the master says 'you are free if I die within one hundred years'?
A) The slave is a mudabbar muqayyad and can be sold.
B) The slave is a mudabbar mutlaq and cannot be sold.
C) The tadbir is invalid entirely.
D) The slave is free immediately upon the statement.

Key Takeaway
Whether a tadbir creates a mudabbar depends on whether freedom is tied unconditionally to death; conditions like 'die or killed' or realistic time limits prevent absolute tadbir, while unrealistic time limits produce absolute tadbir.

8 min
Conditional Tadbir: Death of Master and Another Person
Rulings on declaring a slave free upon the death of master and another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tadbir muqayyad and ta'liq bi-shart and state the ruling on permissibility of sale and source of emancipation (one-third vs. entire estate).

Core Idea
A mudabbar is freed from one-third; a slave freed by a condition not attached to the master's death is freed from the entire estate.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a subtle but crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh: when a master declares his slave free upon his own death together with another condition (like the death of another person), it is considered tadbir muqayyad (restricted tadbir). However, if the condition does not involve the master's death at all, it is a regular conditional suspension (ta'liq bi-shart), not tadbir. This distinction affects both the permissibility of selling the slave and the source of emancipation (from one-third of the estate vs. the entire estate). Let's examine the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, identify the two types of declarations: tadbir muqayyad (freedom attached to master's death plus another condition) and ta'liq bi-shart (freedom attached to a condition unrelated to master's death). In the passage, the first example is 'after my death and the death of so-and-so' (tadbir muqayyad). The second example is 'If so-and-so dies, you are free' (ta'liq bi-shart).
2
Determine the legal effect on permissibility of sale
Both types allow the master to sell the slave before the condition occurs. However, the status differs: in tadbir muqayyad, the slave becomes a mudabbar only after the second condition (death of the other person) occurs. In ta'liq bi-shart, the slave is not a mudabbar at all.
This is the shared ruling that led the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq to mention it in the tadbir chapter.
3
Trace the financial implication upon emancipation
When the condition occurs: a mudabbar (both absolute and restricted) is freed from one-third of the master's estate. A slave freed by a condition not involving the master's death is freed from the entire estate (because the condition takes effect during the master's lifetime, so it is like an immediate gift). If the master dies before the condition, the tadbir remains valid (the slave is freed from one-third at death), but the ta'liq bi-shart becomes void and the slave is not freed at all.
This is the key distinction from another aspect (min jiha ukhra).
4
Apply the distinction to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical declaration, classify it as tadbir or ta'liq, and state the ruling on permissibility of sale and the source of emancipation. For example: 'You are free after my death and after my son's death' – tadbir muqayyad, sale permitted, freed from one-third. 'If my son dies, you are free' – ta'liq bi-shart, sale permitted, freed from entire estate if son dies before master, void if master dies first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معنى الخلافة، فلو مات فلان والمولى حي عتق العبد، وكذلك إن قال أنت حر بعد موتي وموت فلان أو قال بعد موت فلان وموتي لا يكون مدبراً فإن مات فلان قبل المولى فحينئذ يصير مديراً ا هـ.
وفي البدائع : لو قال إن مات فلان فأنت حر لم يكن مدبراً لأنه لم يوجد تعليق عتق عبده بموته فلم يكن هذا تدبيراً بل كان تعليقاً بشرط مطلق كالتعليق بسائر الشروط من دخول الدار وكلام زيد وغير ذلك .اهـ.
فإن قلت : المصنف إنما ذكره في التدبير المقيد لمساواته الحكمه من جواز البيع والعتق بالموت . قلت بينهما فرق من جهة أخرى وهو أن المدبر بقسميه يعتق من الثلث كما قدمناه والمعلق عتقه بشرط غير موت المولى يعتق من جميع المال إذا وجد الشرط ويبطل التعليق بموت المولى قبل وجود الشرط كما لو قال لعبده إن دخلت الدار فأنت فمات المولى قبل الدخول بطلت اليمين ولا يعتق أصلاً بخلاف المدبر .
Meaning of khilafah: if so-and-so dies and the master is alive, the slave is freed. Similarly, if he says, 'You are free after my death and the death of so-and-so', or says 'after the death of so-and-so and my death', he is not a mudabbar. Then if so-and-so dies before the master, at that point he becomes a mudabbar. End. And in al-Bada'i': if he says, 'If so-and-so dies, you are free', he is not a mudabbar, because he did not attach his slave's emancipation to his own death, so this is not tadbir; rather it is a conditional suspension like suspension with other conditions, such as entering the house or the speech of Zayd, etc. End. If you say: the author only mentioned it in restricted tadbir because its rule is equal with regard to permissibility of sale and emancipation at death. I say: there is a difference from another aspect: that the mudabbar in both categories is freed from one-third as we have mentioned, whereas one whose emancipation is suspended by a condition other than the master's death is freed from all the property when the condition occurs, and the suspension becomes void upon the master's death before the condition occurs—as if he said to his slave, 'If you enter the house, you are free' and the master died before entry, the oath becomes void and he is not freed at all, unlike the mudabbar.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with a proof regarding conditional tadbir. The author explains that if a master says to his slave, 'You are free after my death and the death of so-and-so', this is considered tadbir muqayyad (restricted tadbir) because it attaches freedom to the master's death, albeit with an additional condition. The slave becomes a mudabbar only after the other person dies. Al-Bada'i' clarifies that simply saying 'If so-and-so dies, you are free' is not tadbir because it does not attach freedom to the master's death; it is a regular conditional suspension (ta'liq). The author addresses a potential objection: why then did the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq mention this in the chapter on tadbir? The answer is that it shares the ruling of permissibility of sale and emancipation at death. However, a key difference exists: a mudabbar (both absolute and restricted) is freed from one-third of the estate, while a condition not involving the master's death results in freedom from the entire estate (if the condition occurs before the master's death), and if the master dies before the condition, the suspension is void and the slave is not freed. This distinction is crucial for inheritance and property rights.

Key Terms
تدبير مقيد (tadbir muqayyad): A declaration that a slave will be free after the master's death with an additional condition (e.g., death of another person).
تعليق بشرط (ta'liq bi-shart): Suspending emancipation on a condition that is not the master's death, e.g., entering a house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his slave, 'If Zayd dies, you are free,' what is the ruling?
A) The slave becomes a mudabbar immediately.
B) It is not tadbir; it is a regular conditional suspension.
C) It is considered tadbir muqayyad.
D) It is invalid because Zayd is not the master.

Key Takeaway
A declaration that includes the master's death (with or without another condition) is tadbir; otherwise it is ta'liq bi-shart — and they differ in the source of emancipation (one-third vs. entire estate) and the effect of the master's death before the condition.

Conditional Tadbir by a Co-Owner
Ruling on tadbir by one co-owner conditional on both deaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tadbir when one co-owner makes it conditional on the death of both partners, and apply it to determine when the slave becomes mudabbar.

Core Idea
A conditional tadbir by a co-owner only takes effect after one dies, freeing the slave from the survivor.

This passage addresses a nuanced scenario: a jointly owned slave, and one master declares freedom upon the death of both himself and his partner. Does this make the slave a mudabbar immediately? The Hanafi jurists clarify that tadbir requires the death of the master who declared it; since the condition is attached to both deaths, no tadbir occurs until one dies. Then the survivor becomes the sole owner and the mudabbar relationship begins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize that the slave is co-owned equally by two men. One co-owner makes a statement: 'If I die and my partner (meaning the other co-owner) die, you are free.'
The other co-owner may or may not have said anything.
2
Understand the Condition
The tadbir is conditional on two events: the death of the speaker and the death of the partner. Until both die, the condition is not fully met.
The slave's freedom is tied to both deaths.
3
Apply the Immediate Ruling
The slave does not become a mudabbar immediately after the declaration. The reason is that tadbir attaches to the death of the master, but here the condition is not yet fulfilled.
The slave remains a regular co-owned slave.
4
Apply the Ruling After One Death
When one of the co-owners dies, the slave becomes a mudabbar from the surviving co-owner. At that point, the condition for the survivor's tadbir is partially met (the other died), and the survivor's own death becomes the only remaining condition.
The survivor becomes the sole owner by inheritance or otherwise, and the tadbir takes effect.
5
Rationale
The tadbir is valid but suspended. After one death, the survivor owns the slave fully, and the tadbir becomes a valid promise of freedom upon the survivor's death.
If both die simultaneously, the condition fails and no tadbir occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : عبد بين رجلين قال أحدهما إن مت أنا وفلان يعني شريكه فأنت حر لم يكن مدبراً، وكذلك لو قال الآخر مثل ذلك، فإن مات أحدهما صار العبد مدبراً من الآخر اهـ.
And in al-Zahiriyyah: a slave shared between two men; one of them said, 'If I die and so-and-so (meaning his partner) [die], you are free'—he is not a mudabbar. Similarly, if the other said the same. Then if one of them dies, the slave becomes a mudabbar from the other. End.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding tadbir when a slave is jointly owned. If one co-owner declares that the slave will be free upon the death of both himself and his partner, it does not make the slave a mudabbar for either owner immediately. However, if one co-owner dies, then the slave becomes a mudabbar from the surviving co-owner. The reasoning is that tadbir requires attachment to the master's death; here it is conditional on both deaths, so until one dies, the condition is not met. After one dies, the condition becomes possible (the surviving master's death is a future certainty), so tadbir takes effect from the survivor. This is consistent with the previous lesson's principle of conditional tadbir.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A slave is owned jointly by two partners. One says: 'If I and my partner die, you are free.' Which statement is correct?
A) The slave becomes mudabbar from both immediately.
B) The slave becomes mudabbar from the speaker only if the partner dies first.
C) The slave becomes mudabbar from the survivor when one of them dies.
D) The declaration is invalid because it is conditional.

Key Takeaway
A conditional tadbir by one co-owner on the death of both owners only becomes effective after one dies, making the slave a mudabbar from the survivor.

Selling a Mudabbar: Muqayyad vs Mutlaq
Legal reasoning (ta'lil) for a Hanafi ruling on tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a mudabbar muqayyad versus mudabbar mutlaq, explain the reasoning based on the certainty of sabab al-hurriyya, and identify the cross-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
If freedom depends on an uncertain event, sale is allowed; if on certain death, it is not.

In Hanafi law, a mudabbar is a slave whose master has promised freedom upon the master's death. But not all tadbirs are equal. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains why a mudabbar muqayyad (e.g., 'if I die in this journey') can be sold, while a mudabbar mutlaq (e.g., 'after my death') cannot. The key is the certainty of the cause of freedom: uncertain conditions leave the slave fully as property, while certain death creates a strong right to freedom that prevents sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Distinguish mudabbar muqayyad (restricted by a condition) from mudabbar mutlaq (absolute, no condition).
Muqayyad example: 'You are free if I die in this journey.' Mutlaq: 'You are free after my death.'
2
State the ruling for each
Hanafi: Sale of muqayyad is permissible (ja'iz); sale of mutlaq is prohibited.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the cause (sabab al-hurriyya)
The cause of freedom in tadbir is the master's death. In muqayyad, the condition (e.g., dying in a journey) may not occur, so the cause is uncertain. In mutlaq, death is certain.
Uncertainty means the slave's right to freedom is not yet established.
4
Apply the analogy
The muqayyad is likened to other conditional suspensions (ta'liqat) where the condition may fail, so the slave remains fully property. The mutlaq is different because the condition (death) is inevitable.
This is a qiyas on conditional contracts where the condition is uncertain.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Most other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) prohibit sale of any mudabbar, whether muqayyad or mutlaq. The Hanafi position is unique.
The dispute hinges on whether tadbir creates a right of freedom immediately or only upon death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما جاز بيع المدبر المقيد لأن سبب الحرية لم ينعقد في الحال لتردد في هذا القيد لجواز أن لا يموت منه فصار كسائر التعليقات بخلاف المدبر المطلق لأنه تعلق عتقه بمطلق الموت وهو كائن لا محالة.
And the sale of a restricted mudabbar is permitted only because the cause of freedom is not actualized at present, due to uncertainty in this restriction, because it is possible that he will not die from it. Thus it becomes like other conditional suspensions, unlike the absolute mudabbar, because his freedom is attached to absolute death, which will inevitably occur.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a legal reasoning (ta'lil) explaining the difference between restricted and absolute tadbir regarding the permissibility of selling the slave. In restricted tadbir (e.g., 'if I die in this journey'), the cause of freedom—death under that condition—is uncertain. It may not happen, so the slave is not yet fully entitled to freedom. Hence the master may sell him, as the slave remains property. In contrast, absolute tadbir (e.g., 'you are free after my death') attaches freedom to death itself, which is certain. Therefore, the slave is considered to have a strong right to freedom, and selling him is not allowed. This distinction is based on the certainty of the condition.

Key Terms
سبب الحرية (sabab al-hurriyya): The cause that brings about freedom; in tadbir, it is the master's death.
مدبر مقيد (mudabbar muqayyad): A slave whose freedom is tied to a conditional event (e.g., dying in a specific situation).
مدبر مطلق (mudabbar mutlaq): A slave whose freedom is tied to absolute death without condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the sale of a mudabbar muqayyad permissible?
A) Because the master's death is certain.
B) Because the condition for freedom is uncertain, so the slave remains fully property.
C) Because the declaration is invalid until death.
D) Because the slave has not been declared free yet.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of selling a mudabbar hinges on whether the cause of freedom is certain or uncertain.
